class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">54\xc2\xb035\xe2\x80\xb247\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">05\xc2\xb055\xe2\x80\xb248\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">54.59639\xc2\xb0N 5.93000\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">54.59639; -5.93000</span></span></span></a></span></span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Belfast</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xc9\x9b/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">\xc9\x9b</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">BEL</span>-fahst</i></a>; from <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">B\xc3\xa9al Feirste</i>, meaning \'mouth of the sand-bank ford\',<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <small>Irish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Irish" title="Help:IPA/Irish">[b\xca\xb2e\xcb\x90l\xcb\xa0 \xcb\x88f\xca\xb2\xc9\x9b\xc9\xbe\xcb\xa0(\xc9\x99)\xca\x83t\xca\xb2\xc9\x99]</a></span>) is the capital and largest city of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, standing on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/River_Lagan" title="River Lagan">River Lagan</a> on the east coast. It is the 12th-largest city in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and the second-largest on the island of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>. It had a population of 343,542 as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-demography1_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demography1-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Belfast suffered greatly during <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence#North-east" title="Irish War of Independence">the violence</a> that accompanied the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Ireland" title="Partition of Ireland">partition of Ireland</a>, and especially during the more recent conflict known as <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">the Troubles</a>: in the 1970s and 1980s it was one of the world\'s most dangerous cities,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> with a homicide rate around 31 per 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the early 19th century, Belfast was a major <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">port</a>. It played an important role in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> in Ireland, becoming briefly the biggest <a href="/wiki/Linen" title="Linen">linen</a>-producer in the world, earning it the nickname "<a href="/wiki/Linenopolis" title="Linenopolis">Linenopolis</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> By the time it was granted <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom#Northern_Ireland" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status</a> in 1888, it was a major centre of Irish linen production, <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>-processing and rope-making. Shipbuilding was also a key industry; the <a href="/wiki/Harland_and_Wolff" title="Harland and Wolff">Harland and Wolff</a> shipyard, which built the <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" class="mw-redirect" title="RMS Titanic">RMS&#160;<i>Titanic</i></a>, was the world\'s largest shipyard.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Belfast as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> has a major aerospace and missiles industry. <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">Industrialisation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">inward migration</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> it brought, made Belfast Northern Ireland\'s biggest city. Following the partition of Ireland in 1922, Belfast became the seat of government for Northern Ireland. Belfast\'s status as a global industrial centre ended in the decades after the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>.\n</p><p>Belfast is still a port with commercial and industrial docks, including the Harland and Wolff shipyard, dominating the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Lough" title="Belfast Lough">Belfast Lough</a> shoreline. It is served by two airports: <a href="/wiki/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport" title="George Best Belfast City Airport">George Best Belfast City Airport</a>, 3 miles (5 kilometres) from the city centre, and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast International Airport</a> 15 miles (24 kilometres) west of the city. The <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">Globalization and World Cities Research Network (GaWC)</a> listed Belfast as a Gamma + <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li \xe2\x80\x93 sister cities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Freedom_of_the_City"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Freedom of the tocsection-34"><a href="#Military_Units"><span class="tocnumber">14.2</span> <span class="toctext">Military Units</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name Belfast derives from the Irish <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">B\xc3\xa9al Feirsde</i></i>, later spelt <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">B\xc3\xa9al Feirste</i></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Logainm_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Logainm-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The word <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">b\xc3\xa9al</i></i> means "mouth" or "river-mouth" while <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">feirsde/feirste</i></i> is the genitive singular of <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">fearsaid</i></i> and refers to a <a href="/wiki/Shoal" title="Shoal">sandbar</a> or tidal <a href="/wiki/Ford_(crossing)" title="Ford (crossing)">ford</a> across a river\'s mouth.<sup id="cite_ref-Logainm_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Logainm-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_name_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_name-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The name therefore translates literally as "(river) mouth of the sandbar" or "(river) mouth of the ford".<sup id="cite_ref-Logainm_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Logainm-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The sandbar formed at the confluence (at present-day Donegall Quay) of two rivers: the <a href="/wiki/River_Lagan" title="River Lagan">Lagan</a>, which flows into Belfast Lough, and the Lagan\'s tributary the <a href="/wiki/River_Farset" title="River Farset">Farset</a>. This area became the hub around which the original settlement developed.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The Irish name <i><i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text">B\xc3\xa9al Feirste</i></i> is shared by a <a href="/wiki/County_Mayo" title="County Mayo">County Mayo</a> <a href="/wiki/Townland" title="Townland">townland</a> which has the anglicised name  <i>Belfarsad</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An alternative interpretation of the name, "mouth of [the river] of the sandbar", would allude to the River Farset, which flows into the Lagan where the sandbar was located. <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Hogan" title="Edmund Hogan">Edmund Hogan</a><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/John_O%27Donovan_(scholar)" title="John O&#39;Donovan (scholar)">John O\'Donovan</a><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> favoured this interpretation. It seems clear, however, that the river itself took its name from the tidal crossing.<sup id="cite_ref-Logainm_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Logainm-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_dialects" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulster Scots dialects">Ulster-Scots</a>, the name of the city can appear variously written as <i>Bilfawst</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <i>Bilfaust</i><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> or <i>Baelfawst</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> although "Belfast" is also used.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Belfast" title="History of Belfast">History of Belfast</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> of Belfast was created when it was granted city status by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> in 1888,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and the city continues to straddle <a href="/wiki/County_Antrim" title="County Antrim">County Antrim</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_Down" title="County Down">County Down</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The site of Belfast has been occupied since the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Giants_Ring,_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Giants Ring, Belfast">Giant\'s Ring</a>, a 5,000-year-old <a href="/wiki/Henge" title="Henge">henge</a>, is located near the city,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and the remains of <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Hill_fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Hill fort">hill forts</a> can still be seen in the surrounding hills. Belfast remained a small settlement of little importance during the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. <a href="/wiki/John_de_Courcy" title="John de Courcy">John de Courcy</a> built a castle on what is now Castle Street in the city centre in the 12th century, but this was on a lesser scale and not as strategically important as <a href="/wiki/Carrickfergus_Castle" title="Carrickfergus Castle">Carrickfergus Castle</a> to the north, which was built by de Courcy in 1177. The <a href="/wiki/O%27Neill_dynasty" title="O&#39;Neill dynasty">O\'Neill</a> clan had a presence in the area.\n</p><p>In the 14th century, Cloinne Aodha Buidhe, descendants of Aodh Buidhe O\'Neill, built Grey Castle at Castlereagh, now in the east of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Conn O\'Neill of the Clannaboy O\'Neills owned vast lands in the area and was the last inhabitant of Grey Castle, one remaining link being the Conn\'s Water river flowing through east Belfast.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Early_Town">The Early Town</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Early Town">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ground_Plan_of_Belfast_(1685).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ground_Plan_of_Belfast_%281685%29.png/220px-Ground_Plan_of_Belfast_%281685%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ground_Plan_of_Belfast_%281685%29.png/330px-Ground_Plan_of_Belfast_%281685%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ground_Plan_of_Belfast_%281685%29.png/440px-Ground_Plan_of_Belfast_%281685%29.png 2x" data-file-width="3735" data-file-height="2570" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ground_Plan_of_Belfast_(1685).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1685 plan of Belfast by the military engineer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Phillips_(engineer)" title="Thomas Phillips (engineer)">Thomas Phillips</a>, showing the town\'s ramparts and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Castle#Plantation_Castle" title="Belfast Castle">Lord Chichester\'s castle</a>, which was destroyed in a fire in 1708</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bastille-day-belfast-1791.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/40/Bastille-day-belfast-1791.jpg/200px-Bastille-day-belfast-1791.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/40/Bastille-day-belfast-1791.jpg/300px-Bastille-day-belfast-1791.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/40/Bastille-day-belfast-1791.jpg/400px-Bastille-day-belfast-1791.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1804" data-file-height="1381" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bastille-day-belfast-1791.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Volunteer Corps parade down High Street, <a href="/wiki/Bastille_Day" title="Bastille Day">Bastille Day</a>, 1792</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast became a substantial settlement in the 17th century after being established as an English town by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Chichester,_1st_Baron_Chichester" title="Arthur Chichester, 1st Baron Chichester">Sir Arthur Chichester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-belfast_castle_history_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belfast_castle_history-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> As it grew with the port, and with textile manufacture, the English element was overwhelmed by the influx of Scottish Presbyterians. As "Dissenters" from the established Church of Ireland communion, the Presbyterians were conscious of sharing, if only in part, the <a href="/wiki/Penal_Laws" title="Penal Laws">disabilities</a> of Ireland\'s largely dispossessed <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Ireland" title="Catholic Church in Ireland">Roman Catholic</a> majority.\n</p><p>When, in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American War of Independence</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Channel_Naval_Duel" title="North Channel Naval Duel">Belfast Lough was raided</a> by the privateer, <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones" title="John Paul Jones">John Paul Jones</a>, the townspeople assembled their own <a href="/wiki/Irish_Volunteers_(18th_century)" title="Irish Volunteers (18th century)">Volunteer militia</a>. This emboldened a spirit a radical disaffection. Further enthused by the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, the Volunteers and townspeople rallied in support of <a href="/wiki/Catholic_emancipation" title="Catholic emancipation">Catholic emancipation</a> and "a more equal representation of the people" in the Irish Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\nThe two <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament" title="Member of parliament">MPs</a> Belfast returned to Dublin had remained nominees of the Chichesters (<a href="/wiki/Marquess_of_Donegall" title="Marquess of Donegall">Marquesses of Donegall</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In the face of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Ascendancy" title="Protestant Ascendancy">Ascendancy\'s</a> intransigence, these were demands taken up by the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_United_Irishmen" title="Society of United Irishmen">Society of United Irishmen</a> formed at a meeting in the town addressed by <a href="/wiki/Theobald_Wolfe_Tone" class="mw-redirect" title="Theobald Wolfe Tone">Theobald Wolfe Tone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Connolly_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Connolly-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In the expectation of French assistance the Society organised a republican insurrection, defeated to the north and south of Belfast, at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Antrim" title="Battle of Antrim">Antrim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ballynahinch" title="Battle of Ballynahinch">Ballynahinch</a>, in <a href="/wiki/1798_Rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="1798 Rebellion">1798</a>.\n</p><p>Evidence of this period of Belfast\'s growth can still be seen in the oldest areas of the city, known as the <a href="/wiki/The_Belfast_Entries" title="The Belfast Entries">Entries</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Industrial_City">The Industrial City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The Industrial City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:High_Street,_Belfast_(5785358121).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/High_Street%2C_Belfast_%285785358121%29.jpg/220px-High_Street%2C_Belfast_%285785358121%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/High_Street%2C_Belfast_%285785358121%29.jpg/330px-High_Street%2C_Belfast_%285785358121%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/High_Street%2C_Belfast_%285785358121%29.jpg/440px-High_Street%2C_Belfast_%285785358121%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1308" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:High_Street,_Belfast_(5785358121).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>High Street, c. 1906</div></div></div>\n<p>Rapid industrial growth in the nineteenth century drew in landless Catholics from outlying rural and western districts, most settling to the west of the town. The plentiful supply of cheap labour helped attract the English and Scottish capital to Belfast, but it was also a cause of insecurity. Protestant workers organised to protect "their" jobs giving a new lease of life in the town to the once largely rural <a href="/wiki/Orange_Order" title="Orange Order">Orange Order</a>. Sectarian tensions were heightened by movements to <a href="/wiki/Repeal_Association" title="Repeal Association">repeal the Acts of Union</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Irish_Home_Rule_movement" title="Irish Home Rule movement">restore a Parliament</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. Given the progressive enlargement of the British electoral franchise, this would have had an overwhelming Catholic majority and, it was widely believed, interests inimical to the Protestant and industrial north. In 1864 and 1886 the issue had helped trigger deadly sectarian riots.\n</p><p>Sectarian tension was not in itself unique to Belfast: it was shared with Liverpool and Glasgow, cities that following the <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">Great Famine</a> had also experienced large scale Irish Catholic immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> But also common to this "industrial triangle" were traditions of labour militancy. In 1919, workers in all three cities struck for a ten-hour reduction in the working week. In Belfast\xe2\x80\x94notwithstanding the political friction caused by <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/1918_Irish_general_election" title="1918 Irish general election">electoral triumph</a> in the south\xe2\x80\x94this involved some 60,000 workers, Protestant and Catholic, in a four-week walk-out.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a demonstration of their resolve not to submit to a Dublin parliament, in 1912 <a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Hall" title="Belfast City Hall">Belfast City Hall</a> unionists presented the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Covenant" title="Ulster Covenant">Ulster Covenant</a>, which, with an associated Declaration for women, was to accumulate over 470,000 signatures. This was followed by the drilling and eventual arming of a 100,000 strong <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Volunteer_Force" title="Ulster Volunteer Force">Ulster Volunteer Force</a>. The crisis was abated by the onset of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">Great War</a>, the sacrifices of the UVF in which continue to be commemorated in the city (<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Somme Day</a>) by unionist and loyalist organisations.\n</p><p>In 1921, as the greater part of Ireland seceded as the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>, Belfast became the capital of the six counties remaining as <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> in the United Kingdom. In 1932 the devolved parliament for the region was housed in new buildings at <a href="/wiki/Stormont_Buildings" class="mw-redirect" title="Stormont Buildings">Stormont</a> on the eastern edge of the city. In 1920\xe2\x80\x9321, as the two parts of Ireland <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Ireland" title="Partition of Ireland">drew apart</a>, up to 500 people were killed in disturbances in Belfast, the bloodiest period of strife in the city until <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">the Troubles</a> of the late 1960s onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AIR_RAID_DAMAGE_IN_THE_UNITED_KINGDOM_1939-1945_-_H_9476.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/AIR_RAID_DAMAGE_IN_THE_UNITED_KINGDOM_1939-1945_-_H_9476.jpg/220px-AIR_RAID_DAMAGE_IN_THE_UNITED_KINGDOM_1939-1945_-_H_9476.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/AIR_RAID_DAMAGE_IN_THE_UNITED_KINGDOM_1939-1945_-_H_9476.jpg/330px-AIR_RAID_DAMAGE_IN_THE_UNITED_KINGDOM_1939-1945_-_H_9476.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/AIR_RAID_DAMAGE_IN_THE_UNITED_KINGDOM_1939-1945_-_H_9476.jpg/440px-AIR_RAID_DAMAGE_IN_THE_UNITED_KINGDOM_1939-1945_-_H_9476.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="798" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AIR_RAID_DAMAGE_IN_THE_UNITED_KINGDOM_1939-1945_-_H_9476.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aftermath of the Blitz in May 1941</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast was <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Blitz" title="Belfast Blitz">heavily bombed</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Initial raids were a surprise as the city was believed to be outside of the range of German bomber planes. In one raid, in 1941, German bombers killed around one thousand people and left tens of thousands homeless. Apart from London, this was the greatest loss of life in a night raid during the <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">Blitz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Troubles">The Troubles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The Troubles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">The Troubles</a></div>\n<p>Belfast has been the capital of Northern Ireland since its establishment in 1921 following the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland_Act_1920" title="Government of Ireland Act 1920">Government of Ireland Act 1920</a>. It had been the scene of various episodes of sectarian conflict between its Catholic and Protestant populations. These opposing groups in this conflict are now often termed <a href="/wiki/Irish_republicanism" title="Irish republicanism">republican</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ulster_loyalism" title="Ulster loyalism">loyalist</a> respectively, although they are also loosely referred to as \'<a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">nationalist</a>\' and \'<a href="/wiki/Unionism_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Unionism (Ireland)">unionist</a>\'. The most recent example of this conflict was known as the Troubles \xe2\x80\x93 a civil conflict that raged from around 1969 to 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_trouble_history_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_trouble_history-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shankilltroubles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Shankilltroubles.jpg/220px-Shankilltroubles.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Shankilltroubles.jpg/330px-Shankilltroubles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Shankilltroubles.jpg/440px-Shankilltroubles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="998" data-file-height="646" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shankilltroubles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Shankill_Road" title="Shankill Road">Shankill Road</a> during the Troubles, 1970s</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast saw some of the worst of the Troubles in Northern Ireland, particularly in the 1970s, with rival paramilitary groups formed on both sides. Bombing, assassination and street violence formed a backdrop to life throughout the Troubles. In December 1971, 15 people, including two children, were killed when the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Volunteer_Force" title="Ulster Volunteer Force">Ulster Volunteer Force</a> (UVF) <a href="/wiki/McGurk%27s_Bar_bombing" title="McGurk&#39;s Bar bombing">bombed McGurk\'s Bar</a>, the greatest loss of life in a single incident in Belfast.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Loyalist paramilitaries including the UVF and the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Defence_Association" title="Ulster Defence Association">Ulster Defence Association</a> (UDA) said that the killings they carried out were in retaliation for the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_IRA_campaign_1969%E2%80%931997" class="mw-redirect" title="Provisional IRA campaign 1969\xe2\x80\x931997">IRA campaign</a>. Most of their victims were Catholics with no links to the Provisional IRA.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> A particularly notorious group, based on the <a href="/wiki/Shankill_Road" title="Shankill Road">Shankill Road</a> in the mid-1970s, became known as the <a href="/wiki/Shankill_Butchers" title="Shankill Butchers">Shankill Butchers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Provisional_IRA" class="mw-redirect" title="Provisional IRA">Provisional IRA</a> detonated 22 bombs within the confines of Belfast city centre on 21 July 1972, on what is known as <a href="/wiki/Bloody_Friday_(1972)" title="Bloody Friday (1972)">Bloody Friday</a>, killing nine people.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the Troubles the <a href="/wiki/Europa_Hotel,_Belfast" title="Europa Hotel, Belfast">Europa Hotel</a> suffered 36 bomb attacks becoming known as "the most bombed hotel in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In all, over 1,600 people were killed in political violence in the city between 1969 and 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Belfast_city_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast city centre">Belfast city centre</a> has undergone expansion and regeneration since the late 1990s, notably around <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Square_(Belfast)" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Square (Belfast)">Victoria Square</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In late 2018, it was announced that Belfast would undergo a \xc2\xa3500&#160;million urban regeneration project known as "Tribeca" on a large city centre site.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> However, tensions and civil disturbances still occur despite the 1998 peace agreement, including sectarian riots and paramilitary attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belfast and the <a href="/wiki/Causeway_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Causeway Coast">Causeway Coast</a> were together named the best place to visit in 2018 by <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Tourist numbers have increased since the end of <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">The Troubles</a>, boosted in part by newer attractions such as <a href="/wiki/Titanic_Belfast" title="Titanic Belfast">Titanic Belfast</a> and tours of locations used in the <a href="/wiki/Home_Box_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Box Office">HBO</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Belfast.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flag_of_Belfast.svg/220px-Flag_of_Belfast.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flag_of_Belfast.svg/330px-Flag_of_Belfast.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flag_of_Belfast.svg/440px-Flag_of_Belfast.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="420" data-file-height="250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Belfast.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of Belfast</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast was granted <a href="/wiki/Borough_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Borough status in the United Kingdom">borough status</a> by <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI and I</a> in 1613 and official <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status</a> by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> in 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Since 1973 it has been a <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_(Boundaries)_Act_(Northern_Ireland)_1971" title="Local Government (Boundaries) Act (Northern Ireland) 1971">local government district</a> under local administration by <a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Council" title="Belfast City Council">Belfast City Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Belfast is represented in both the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">British House of Commons</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a>. For elections to the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, Belfast was within the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="Northern Ireland (European Parliament constituency)">Northern Ireland constituency</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Council" title="Belfast City Council">Belfast City Council</a></div>\n<p>Belfast City Council is the <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Local government in Northern Ireland">local council</a> with responsibility for the city. The city\'s elected officials are the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor_of_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor of Belfast">Lord Mayor of Belfast</a>, Deputy Lord Mayor and <a href="/wiki/High_Sheriff" class="mw-redirect" title="High Sheriff">High Sheriff</a> who are elected from among 60 <a href="/wiki/Councillors" class="mw-redirect" title="Councillors">councillors</a>. The first Lord Mayor of Belfast was <a href="/wiki/Sir_Daniel_Dixon,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir Daniel Dixon, 1st Baronet">Daniel Dixon</a>, who was elected in 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_City_Council_\xe2\x80\x93_Lord_Mayor_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_City_Council_\xe2\x80\x93_Lord_Mayor-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor">Lord Mayor</a> for 2019\xe2\x80\x9320 is John Finucane <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a>, while the Deputy Lord Mayor is an <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Party_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Alliance Party of Northern Ireland">Alliance Party of Northern Ireland</a> councillor. The Lord Mayor\'s duties include presiding over meetings of the council, receiving distinguished visitors to the city, representing and promoting the city on the national and international stage.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_City_Council_\xe2\x80\x93_Lord_Mayor_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_City_Council_\xe2\x80\x93_Lord_Mayor-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_City_Hall_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Belfast_City_Hall_2.jpg/220px-Belfast_City_Hall_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Belfast_City_Hall_2.jpg/330px-Belfast_City_Hall_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Belfast_City_Hall_2.jpg/440px-Belfast_City_Hall_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="677" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_City_Hall_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Hall" title="Belfast City Hall">Belfast City Hall</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1997, <a href="/wiki/Unionism_in_Ireland" title="Unionism in Ireland">unionists</a> lost overall control of Belfast City Council for the first time in its history, with the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Party_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Alliance Party of Northern Ireland">Alliance Party of Northern Ireland</a> gaining the balance of power between <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">nationalists</a> and unionists. This position was confirmed in four subsequent council elections, with mayors from Sinn F\xc3\xa9in and the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_and_Labour_Party" title="Social Democratic and Labour Party">Social Democratic and Labour Party</a> (SDLP), both of whom are nationalist parties, and the cross-community Alliance Party regularly elected since. The first nationalist Lord Mayor of Belfast was Alban Maginness of the SDLP, in 1997.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Ireland_Assembly_and_Westminster">Northern Ireland Assembly and Westminster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Northern Ireland Assembly and Westminster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stormont_Parliament_Buildings_during_Giro_d%27Italia,_May_2014(6).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Stormont_Parliament_Buildings_during_Giro_d%27Italia%2C_May_2014%286%29.jpg/220px-Stormont_Parliament_Buildings_during_Giro_d%27Italia%2C_May_2014%286%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Stormont_Parliament_Buildings_during_Giro_d%27Italia%2C_May_2014%286%29.jpg/330px-Stormont_Parliament_Buildings_during_Giro_d%27Italia%2C_May_2014%286%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Stormont_Parliament_Buildings_during_Giro_d%27Italia%2C_May_2014%286%29.jpg/440px-Stormont_Parliament_Buildings_during_Giro_d%27Italia%2C_May_2014%286%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4338" data-file-height="2932" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stormont_Parliament_Buildings_during_Giro_d%27Italia,_May_2014(6).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Parliament_Buildings_(Northern_Ireland)" title="Parliament Buildings (Northern Ireland)">Stormont</a> is home to the Northern Ireland Assembly.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Belfast_(Northern_Ireland_Parliament_constituencies)" title="Belfast (Northern Ireland Parliament constituencies)">Belfast (Northern Ireland Parliament constituencies)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast (UK Parliament constituency)">Belfast (UK Parliament constituency)</a></div>\n<p>As Northern Ireland\'s capital city, Belfast is host to the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a> at <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Buildings_(Northern_Ireland)" title="Parliament Buildings (Northern Ireland)">Stormont</a>, the site of the <a href="/wiki/Devolution#Northern_Ireland" title="Devolution">devolved</a> legislature for Northern Ireland. Belfast is divided into four <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">UK parliamentary</a> constituencies: <a href="/wiki/Belfast_North_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast North (UK Parliament constituency)">Belfast North</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belfast_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast West (UK Parliament constituency)">Belfast West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belfast_South_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast South (UK Parliament constituency)">Belfast South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast East (UK Parliament constituency)">Belfast East</a>. All four extend beyond the city boundaries to include parts of <a href="/wiki/Castlereagh_(borough)" title="Castlereagh (borough)">Castlereagh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisburn_City_Council" title="Lisburn City Council">Lisburn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newtownabbey_Borough_Council" title="Newtownabbey Borough Council">Newtownabbey</a> districts. In the <a href="/wiki/2017_Northern_Ireland_Assembly_election" title="2017 Northern Ireland Assembly election">Northern Ireland Assembly Elections in 2017</a>, Belfast elected 20 <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_Legislative_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of the Legislative Assembly">Members of the Legislative Assembly</a> (MLAs), 5 from each <a href="/wiki/List_of_Parliamentary_constituencies_in_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Parliamentary constituencies in Northern Ireland">constituency</a>. Belfast elected 7 <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a>, 5 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Unionist_Party" title="Democratic Unionist Party">DUP</a>, 2 <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_and_Labour_Party" title="Social Democratic and Labour Party">SDLP</a>, 3 <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Party_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Alliance Party of Northern Ireland">Alliance Party</a>, 1 <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Unionist_Party" title="Ulster Unionist Party">UUP</a>, 1 <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_in_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Party in Northern Ireland">Green</a> and 1 <a href="/wiki/People_Before_Profit_Alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="People Before Profit Alliance">PBPA</a> MLAs.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In the 2017 UK general election, Belfast elected one <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament_(United_Kingdom)" title="Member of Parliament (United Kingdom)">MP</a> from each constituency to the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> at Westminster, London. This comprised 3 DUP and 1 Sinn F\xc3\xa9in. In the <a href="/wiki/2019_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2019 United Kingdom general election">2019 UK general election</a>, the DUP lost two of their seats in Belfast; to Sinn F\xc3\xa9in in North Belfast and to the SDLP in South Belfast.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_Aerial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Aerial photo of urban sprawl, edged by green hills and sea shore, and bisected by a winding river." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Belfast_Aerial.jpg/220px-Belfast_Aerial.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Belfast_Aerial.jpg/330px-Belfast_Aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Belfast_Aerial.jpg/440px-Belfast_Aerial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_Aerial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Belfast.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_with_Lough_by_Sentinel-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Belfast_with_Lough_by_Sentinel-2.jpg/220px-Belfast_with_Lough_by_Sentinel-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Belfast_with_Lough_by_Sentinel-2.jpg/330px-Belfast_with_Lough_by_Sentinel-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Belfast_with_Lough_by_Sentinel-2.jpg/440px-Belfast_with_Lough_by_Sentinel-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4997" data-file-height="3619" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_with_Lough_by_Sentinel-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite image of Belfast with Lough</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast is at the western end of Belfast Lough and at the mouth of the River Lagan giving it the ideal location for the shipbuilding industry that once made it famous. When the <i><a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" class="mw-redirect" title="RMS Titanic">Titanic</a></i> was built in Belfast in 1911\xe2\x80\x931912, <a href="/wiki/Harland_and_Wolff" title="Harland and Wolff">Harland and Wolff</a> had the largest shipyard in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Titanic_in_History_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Titanic_in_History-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\nBelfast is situated on Northern Ireland\'s eastern <a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">coast</a> at <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994658806"/><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Belfast&amp;params=54_35_49_N_05_55_45_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">54\xc2\xb035\xe2\x80\xb249\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">05\xc2\xb055\xe2\x80\xb245\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">54.59694\xc2\xb0N 5.92917\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">54.59694; -5.92917</span></span></span></a></span>. A consequence of this northern latitude is that it both endures short winter days and enjoys long summer evenings. During the <a href="/wiki/Winter_solstice" title="Winter solstice">winter solstice</a>, the shortest day of the year, local sunset is before 16:00 while sunrise is around 08:45. This is balanced by the <a href="/wiki/Solstice" title="Solstice">summer solstice</a> in June, when the sun sets after 22:00 and rises before 05:00.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1994, a <a href="/wiki/Lagan_Weir" title="Lagan Weir">weir</a> was built across the river by the <a href="/wiki/Laganside_Corporation" title="Laganside Corporation">Laganside Corporation</a> to raise the average water level so that it would cover the unseemly mud flats which gave Belfast its name<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> (from&#32;<a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>&#32;<i> B\xc3\xa9al Feirste</i>&#160;\'The sandy ford at the river mouth\').<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_name_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_name-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The area of Belfast Local Government District is 42.31 square miles (109.6&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-Areameasurements_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Areameasurements-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/River_Farset" title="River Farset">River Farset</a> is also named after this <a href="/wiki/Silt" title="Silt">silt</a> deposit (from the Irish <i>feirste</i> meaning "sand spit"). Originally a more significant river than it is today, the Farset formed a dock on High Street until the mid 19th century. Bank Street in the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Centre" title="Belfast City Centre">city centre</a> referred to the river bank and Bridge Street was named for the site of an early Farset bridge.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Superseded by the River Lagan as the more important river in the city, the Farset now languishes in obscurity, under High Street. There are no less than twelve other minor rivers in and around Belfast, namely the Blackstaff, the Colin, the Connswater, the Cregagh, the Derriaghy, the Forth, the Knock, the Legoniel, the Loop, the Milewater, the Purdysburn and the Ravernet.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cavehill,_Belfast.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Cavehill%2C_Belfast.jpg/220px-Cavehill%2C_Belfast.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Cavehill%2C_Belfast.jpg/330px-Cavehill%2C_Belfast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Cavehill%2C_Belfast.jpg/440px-Cavehill%2C_Belfast.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cavehill,_Belfast.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cavehill" title="Cavehill">Cavehill</a>, a basaltic hill overlooking the city</div></div></div>\n<p>The city is flanked on the north and northwest by a series of hills, including <a href="/wiki/Divis" title="Divis">Divis Mountain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Mountain_(Belfast)" title="Black Mountain (Belfast)">Black Mountain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cavehill" title="Cavehill">Cavehill</a>, thought to be the inspiration for <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Swift" title="Jonathan Swift">Jonathan Swift</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Gulliver%27s_Travels" title="Gulliver&#39;s Travels">Gulliver\'s Travels</a></i>. When Swift was living at Lilliput Cottage near the bottom of Belfast\'s Limestone Road, he imagined that the Cavehill resembled the shape of a sleeping giant safeguarding the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Jonathan_Swift_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jonathan_Swift-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The shape of the giant\'s nose, known locally as <i>Napoleon\'s Nose</i>, is officially called McArt\'s Fort probably named after Art O\'Neill, a 17th-century chieftain who controlled the area at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Castlereagh_(borough)" title="Castlereagh (borough)">Castlereagh</a> Hills overlook the city on the southeast.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As with the vast majority of the rest of Ireland, Belfast has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<i>Cfb</i> in the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a>), with a narrow range of temperatures and rainfall throughout the year. The climate of Belfast is significantly milder than most other locations in the world at a similar latitude, due to the warming influence of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>. There are currently five weather observing stations in the Belfast area: <a href="/wiki/Helen%27s_Bay" title="Helen&#39;s Bay">Helen\'s Bay</a>, Stormont, Newforge, Castlereagh, and Ravenhill Road. Slightly further afield is Aldergrove Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The highest temperature recorded at any official weather station in the Belfast area was 30.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (87.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F) at <a href="/wiki/Shaw%27s_Bridge" title="Shaw&#39;s Bridge">Shaw\'s Bridge</a> on 12 July 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-Met_Office_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Met_Office-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city gets significant precipitation (greater than 1mm) on 157 days in an average year with an average annual rainfall of 846 millimetres (33.3&#160;in),<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Weather_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Weather-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> less than areas of northern England or most of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Met_Office_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Met_Office-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> but higher than <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> or the south-east coast of Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> As an urban and coastal area, Belfast typically gets snow on fewer than 10 days per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Met_Office_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Met_Office-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The absolute maximum temperature at the weather station at Stormont is 29.7&#160;\xc2\xb0C (85.5&#160;\xc2\xb0F), set during July 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In an average year the warmest day will rise to a temperature of 25.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C (77.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F)<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> with a day of 25.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (77.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F) or above occurring roughly once every two in three years.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The absolute minimum temperature at Stormont is \xe2\x88\x929.9&#160;\xc2\xb0C (14&#160;\xc2\xb0F), during January 1982,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> although in an average year the coldest night will fall no lower than \xe2\x88\x924.5&#160;\xc2\xb0C (23.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F) with air frost being recorded on just 26 nights.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The lowest temperature to occur in recent years was \xe2\x88\x928.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C (16.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F) on 22 December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The nearest weather station for which sunshine data and longer term observations are available is <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/Aldergrove,_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Aldergrove, Northern Ireland">Aldergrove</a>). Temperature extremes here have slightly more variability due to the more inland location. The average warmest day at Aldergrove for example will reach a temperature of 25.4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (77.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F),<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> (1.0&#160;\xc2\xb0C [1.8&#160;\xc2\xb0F] higher than Stormont) and 2.1 days<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> should attain a temperature of 25.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C (77.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F) or above in total. Conversely the coldest night of the year averages \xe2\x88\x926.9&#160;\xc2\xb0C (19.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F)<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> (or 1.9&#160;\xc2\xb0C [3.4&#160;\xc2\xb0F] lower than Stormont) and 39 nights should register an air frost.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Some 13 more frosty nights than Stormont. The minimum temperature at Aldergrove was \xe2\x88\x9214.9&#160;\xc2\xb0C (5.2&#160;\xc2\xb0F), during December 2010.\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:100%;
