class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n<p><br />\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Areas_and_districts">Areas and districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Areas and districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Belfast" title="Subdivisions of Belfast">Subdivisions of Belfast</a></div><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information&#32;on City Layout: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Belfast#City_layout" title="Transport in Belfast">Transport in Belfast \xc2\xa7&#160;City layout</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RoyalAvenueBelfast.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/RoyalAvenueBelfast.jpg/220px-RoyalAvenueBelfast.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/RoyalAvenueBelfast.jpg/330px-RoyalAvenueBelfast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/RoyalAvenueBelfast.jpg/440px-RoyalAvenueBelfast.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4592" data-file-height="2576" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RoyalAvenueBelfast.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royal Avenue</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_townlands_in_Belfast" title="List of townlands in Belfast">townlands of Belfast</a> are its oldest surviving land divisions and most pre-date the city. Belfast expanded very rapidly from being a market town to becoming an industrial city during the course of the 19th century. Because of this, it is less an agglomeration of villages and towns which have expanded into each other, than other comparable cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> or <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>. The city expanded to the natural barrier of the hills that surround it, overwhelming other settlements. Consequently, the arterial roads along which this expansion took place (such as the <a href="/wiki/Falls_Road,_Belfast" title="Falls Road, Belfast">Falls Road</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Newtownards_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="Newtownards Road">Newtownards Road</a>) are more significant in defining the districts of the city than nucleated settlements. <a href="/wiki/Segregation_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Segregation in Northern Ireland">Parts of Belfast are segregated</a> by walls, commonly known as "<a href="/wiki/Peace_lines" title="Peace lines">peace lines</a>", erected by the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> after August 1969, and which still divide 14 districts in the inner city.<sup id="cite_ref-Peacelines_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peacelines-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In 2008 a process was proposed for the removal of the \'peace walls\'.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In June 2007, a <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>16&#160;million programme was announced which will transform and redevelop streets and public spaces in the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Major arterial roads (<a href="/wiki/Quality_bus_corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="Quality bus corridor">quality bus corridor</a>) into the city include the <a href="/wiki/Antrim_Road" title="Antrim Road">Antrim Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shore_Road,_Belfast" title="Shore Road, Belfast">Shore Road</a>, Holywood Road, Newtownards Road, Castlereagh Road, Cregagh Road, <a href="/wiki/Ormeau_Road" title="Ormeau Road">Ormeau Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malone_Road" title="Malone Road">Malone Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisburn_Road" title="Lisburn Road">Lisburn Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falls_Road,_Belfast" title="Falls Road, Belfast">Falls Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Springfield_Road,_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Springfield Road, Belfast">Springfield Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shankill_Road" title="Shankill Road">Shankill Road</a>, and Crumlin Road, Four Winds.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_St._Anne_Belfast.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Cathedral_St._Anne_Belfast.jpg/220px-Cathedral_St._Anne_Belfast.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Cathedral_St._Anne_Belfast.jpg/330px-Cathedral_St._Anne_Belfast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Cathedral_St._Anne_Belfast.jpg/440px-Cathedral_St._Anne_Belfast.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_St._Anne_Belfast.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St Anne\'s Cathedral</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast city centre is divided into two postcode districts, <i>BT1</i> for the area lying north of the City Hall, and <i>BT2</i> for the area to its south. The industrial estate and docklands <i>BT3</i>. The rest of the Belfast <a href="/wiki/Post_town" title="Post town">post town</a> is divided in a broadly <a href="/wiki/Clockwise" title="Clockwise">clockwise</a> system from <i>BT3</i> in the north-east round to <i>BT15</i>, with <i>BT16</i> and <i>BT17</i> further out to the east and west respectively. Although <i>BT</i> derives from <i>Belfast</i>, the <a href="/wiki/BT_postcode_area" title="BT postcode area">BT postcode area</a> extends across the whole of Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2001, boosted by increasing numbers of tourists, the city council has developed a number of cultural <a href="/wiki/Belfast_quarters" title="Belfast quarters">quarters</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Quarter,_Belfast" title="Cathedral Quarter, Belfast">Cathedral Quarter</a> takes its name from <a href="/wiki/St_Anne%27s_Cathedral,_Belfast" title="St Anne&#39;s Cathedral, Belfast">St Anne\'s Cathedral</a> (<a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ireland" title="Church of Ireland">Church of Ireland</a>) and has taken on the mantle of the city\'s key cultural locality.<sup id="cite_ref-Cathedral_Quarter_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cathedral_Quarter-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> It hosts a yearly <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Quarter_Arts_Festival" title="Cathedral Quarter Arts Festival">visual and performing arts festival</a>.\n</p><p>Custom House Square is one of the city\'s main outdoor venues for free concerts and street entertainment. The <a href="/wiki/Gaeltacht_Quarter,_Belfast" title="Gaeltacht Quarter, Belfast">Gaeltacht Quarter</a> is an area around the Falls Road in west Belfast which promotes and encourages the use of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Quarter,_Belfast" title="Queen&#39;s Quarter, Belfast">Queen\'s Quarter</a> in south Belfast is named after <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University_Belfast" title="Queen&#39;s University Belfast">Queen\'s University</a>. The area has a large student population and hosts the annual <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Festival_at_Queen%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Festival at Queen&#39;s">Belfast International Arts Festival</a> each autumn. It is home to <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Botanic_Gardens" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Botanic Gardens">Botanic Gardens</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Museum" title="Ulster Museum">Ulster Museum</a>, which was reopened in 2009 after major redevelopment.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Golden_Mile_(Belfast)" title="Golden Mile (Belfast)">The Golden Mile</a> is the name given to the mile between Belfast City Hall and Queen\'s University. Taking in Dublin Road, <a href="/wiki/Great_Victoria_Street,_Belfast" title="Great Victoria Street, Belfast">Great Victoria Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaftesbury_Square" title="Shaftesbury Square">Shaftesbury Square</a> and Bradbury Place, it contains some of the best bars and restaurants in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> in 1998, the nearby Lisburn Road has developed into the city\'s most exclusive shopping strip.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Finally, the <a href="/wiki/Titanic_Quarter,_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Titanic Quarter, Belfast">Titanic Quarter</a> covers 0.75&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (185 acres) of reclaimed land adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Belfast">Belfast Harbour</a>, formerly known as <i>Queen\'s Island</i>. Named after  <i><a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" class="mw-redirect" title="RMS Titanic">RMS Titanic</a></i>, which was built here in 1912,<sup id="cite_ref-Titanic_in_History_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Titanic_in_History-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> work has begun which promises to transform some former shipyard land into "one of the largest waterfront developments in Europe".<sup id="cite_ref-Titanic_Quarter_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Titanic_Quarter-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Plans include apartments, a riverside entertainment district, and a major Titanic-themed museum.<sup id="cite_ref-Titanic_Quarter_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Titanic_Quarter-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In its 2018 report on Best Places to Live in Britain, <i>The Sunday Times</i> named Ballyhackamore, "the brunch capital of Belfast", as the best place in Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The district of Ballyhackamore has even acquired the name "Ballysnackamore" due to the preponderance of dining establishments in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:City_Quays.jpg" class="image" title="City quays panorama"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/City_Quays.jpg/800px-City_Quays.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="243" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/City_Quays.jpg/1200px-City_Quays.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/City_Quays.jpg/1600px-City_Quays.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5998" data-file-height="1819" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_Quays.jpg" title="File:City Quays.jpg"> </a></div>City quays panorama</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Belfast" title="Architecture of Belfast">Architecture of Belfast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buildings_and_structures_in_Belfast" title="Buildings and structures in Belfast">Buildings and structures in Belfast</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_and_structures_in_Belfast" title="List of tallest buildings and structures in Belfast">List of tallest buildings and structures in Belfast</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_public_art_in_Belfast" title="List of public art in Belfast">List of public art in Belfast</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Obel_Tower_completed.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Obel_Tower_completed.jpg/170px-Obel_Tower_completed.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Obel_Tower_completed.jpg/255px-Obel_Tower_completed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Obel_Tower_completed.jpg/340px-Obel_Tower_completed.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Obel_Tower_completed.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Obel_Tower" title="Obel Tower">Obel Tower</a> is the tallest building in Belfast and Ireland.</div></div></div>\n<p>The architectural style of Belfast\'s public buildings range from a small set of <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> buildings, many examples of <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian</a>, including the main <i>Lanyon Building</i> at <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University_Belfast" title="Queen&#39;s University Belfast">Queen\'s University Belfast</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Linenhall_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Linenhall Library">Linenhall Library</a>, (both designed by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lanyon" title="Charles Lanyon">Sir Charles Lanyon</a>). There are also many examples of <a href="/wiki/Edwardian_Baroque_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Edwardian Baroque architecture">Edwardian</a>, such as the City Hall, to modern, such as the <a href="/wiki/Waterfront_Hall" title="Waterfront Hall">Waterfront Hall</a>.\n</p><p>The City Hall was finished in 1906 and was built to reflect Belfast\'s city status, granted by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> in 1888. The <a href="/wiki/Edwardian_Baroque_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Edwardian Baroque architecture">Edwardian</a> architectural style of Belfast City Hall influenced the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Memorial_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Memorial (India)">Victoria Memorial</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Calcutta</a>, India, and <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a> City Hall in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The dome is 173&#160;ft (53&#160;m) high and figures above the door state "<a href="/wiki/Hibernia" title="Hibernia">Hibernia</a> encouraging and promoting the Commerce and Arts of the City".<sup id="cite_ref-Go_To_Historic_Buildings_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Go_To_Historic_Buildings-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Among the city\'s grandest buildings are two former banks: <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Bank" title="Ulster Bank">Ulster Bank</a> in Waring Street (built in 1860) and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Bank">Northern Bank</a>, in nearby Donegall Street (built in 1769). The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Courts_of_Justice,_Belfast" title="Royal Courts of Justice, Belfast">Royal Courts of Justice</a> in Chichester Street are home to Northern Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/Courts_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Courts of Northern Ireland">Supreme Court</a>. Many of Belfast\'s oldest buildings are found in the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Quarter,_Belfast" title="Cathedral Quarter, Belfast">Cathedral Quarter</a> area, which is currently undergoing redevelopment as the city\'s main cultural and tourist area.<sup id="cite_ref-Cathedral_Quarter_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cathedral_Quarter-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Windsor House, 262&#160;ft (80&#160;m) high, has 23 floors and is the second tallest building (as distinct from structure) in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Work has started on the taller <a href="/wiki/Obel_Tower" title="Obel Tower">Obel Tower</a>, which already surpasses the height of Windsor House in its unfinished state.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Provident_Institution,_Belfast.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Scottish_Provident_Institution%2C_Belfast.jpg/220px-Scottish_Provident_Institution%2C_Belfast.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Scottish_Provident_Institution%2C_Belfast.jpg/330px-Scottish_Provident_Institution%2C_Belfast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Scottish_Provident_Institution%2C_Belfast.jpg/440px-Scottish_Provident_Institution%2C_Belfast.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Provident_Institution,_Belfast.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scottish Provident Institution, an example of <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian architecture</a> in Belfast</div></div></div>\n<p>The ornately decorated <a href="/wiki/The_Crown_Liquor_Saloon" class="mw-redirect" title="The Crown Liquor Saloon">Crown Liquor Saloon</a>, designed by Joseph Anderson in 1876, in Great Victoria Street is one of only two pubs in the UK that are owned by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Trust_properties_in_Northern_Ireland" title="List of National Trust properties in Northern Ireland">National Trust</a> (the other is <a href="/wiki/The_George_Inn,_Southwark" title="The George Inn, Southwark">the George Inn, Southwark</a> in London). It was made internationally famous as the setting for the classic film, <i><a href="/wiki/Odd_Man_Out" title="Odd Man Out">Odd Man Out</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/James_Mason" title="James Mason">James Mason</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The restaurant panels in the Crown Bar were originally made for <i>Britannic</i>, the sister ship of the <i>Titanic</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Go_To_Historic_Buildings_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Go_To_Historic_Buildings-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> built in Belfast.\n</p><p>The Harland and Wolff shipyard has two of the largest <a href="/wiki/Dry_dock" title="Dry dock">dry docks</a> in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> where the giant cranes, <a href="/wiki/Samson_and_Goliath_(cranes)" title="Samson and Goliath (cranes)">Samson and Goliath</a> stand out against Belfast\'s skyline.\nIncluding the Waterfront Hall and the <a href="/wiki/Odyssey_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Odyssey Arena">Odyssey Arena</a>, Belfast has several other venues for performing arts. The architecture of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Opera_House_(Belfast)" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Opera House (Belfast)">Grand Opera House</a> has an oriental theme and was completed in 1895. It was bombed several times during the Troubles but has now been restored to its former glory.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lyric_Players%27_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyric Players&#39; Theatre">The Lyric Theatre</a>, (re-opened 1 May 2011 after undergoing a rebuilding programme) the only full-time producing theatre in the country, is where film star <a href="/wiki/Liam_Neeson" title="Liam Neeson">Liam Neeson</a> began his career.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Hall" title="Ulster Hall">Ulster Hall</a> (1859\xe2\x80\x931862) was originally designed for grand dances but is now used primarily as a concert and sporting venue. <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George" title="David Lloyd George">Lloyd George</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_Parnell" title="Charles Stewart Parnell">Parnell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Pearse" title="Patrick Pearse">Patrick Pearse</a> all attended political rallies there.<sup id="cite_ref-Go_To_Historic_Buildings_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Go_To_Historic_Buildings-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A legacy of <a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">the Troubles</a> are the many \'<a href="/wiki/Peace_lines" title="Peace lines">peace lines</a>\' or \'<a href="/wiki/Peace_Walls" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace Walls">peace walls</a>\' that still act as barriers to reinforce ethno-sectarian residential segregation in the city.  In 2017, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.belfastinterfaceproject.org">Belfast Interface Project</a> published a study entitled \'<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.belfastinterfaceproject.org/sites/default/files/publications/Interfaces%20PDF.pdf">Interface Barriers, Peacelines &amp; Defensive Architecture</a>\' that identified 97 separate walls, barriers and interfaces in Belfast.  A history of the development of these structures can be found at the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.peacewall-archive.net">Peacewall Archive</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_gardens">Parks and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Parks and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_parks_and_gardens_in_Belfast" title="List of parks and gardens in Belfast">List of parks and gardens in Belfast</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flower_bed,_Botanic_Gardens,_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1454550.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Flower_bed%2C_Botanic_Gardens%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1454550.jpg/220px-Flower_bed%2C_Botanic_Gardens%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1454550.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Flower_bed%2C_Botanic_Gardens%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1454550.jpg/330px-Flower_bed%2C_Botanic_Gardens%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1454550.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Flower_bed%2C_Botanic_Gardens%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1454550.jpg/440px-Flower_bed%2C_Botanic_Gardens%2C_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1454550.jpg 2x" data-file-width="635" data-file-height="391" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flower_bed,_Botanic_Gardens,_Belfast_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1454550.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Palm House at the <a href="/wiki/Botanic_Gardens_(Belfast)" title="Botanic Gardens (Belfast)">Botanic Gardens</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Sitting at the mouth of the River Lagan where it becomes a deep and sheltered lough, Belfast is surrounded by mountains that create a micro-climate conducive to horticulture. From the Victorian Botanic Gardens in the heart of the city to the heights of Cave Hill Country Park, the great expanse of <a href="/wiki/Lagan_Valley" title="Lagan Valley">Lagan Valley</a> Regional Park<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> to Colin Glen, Belfast contains an abundance of parkland and forest parks.<sup id="cite_ref-Parks_and_gardens_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parks_and_gardens-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Parks and gardens are an integral part of Belfast\'s heritage, and home to an abundance of local wildlife and popular places for a picnic, a stroll or a jog. Numerous events take place throughout including festivals such as Rose Week and special activities such as bird watching evenings and great beast hunts.<sup id="cite_ref-Parks_and_gardens_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parks_and_gardens-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belfast has over forty public parks. The Forest of Belfast is a partnership between government and local groups, set up in 1992 to manage and conserve the city\'s parks and open spaces. They have commissioned more than 30 public sculptures since 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Council" title="Belfast City Council">City Council</a> set aside \xc2\xa38&#160;million to continue this work.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Naturalists%27_Field_Club" title="Belfast Naturalists&#39; Field Club">Belfast Naturalists\' Field Club</a> was founded in 1863 and is administered by National Museums and Galleries of Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:City_Quays_Rec.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A picture of a recreational ground with a sculpture of a salmon and a building in the background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/City_Quays_Rec.jpg/220px-City_Quays_Rec.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/City_Quays_Rec.jpg/330px-City_Quays_Rec.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/City_Quays_Rec.jpg/440px-City_Quays_Rec.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4056" data-file-height="3057" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:City_Quays_Rec.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A recreation ground next to the <a href="/wiki/Obel_Tower" title="Obel Tower">Obel Tower</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Salmon_of_Knowledge" title="Salmon of Knowledge">Salmon of Knowledge</a> is visible on the left.</div></div></div>\n<p>With an average of 670,000 visitors per year between 2007 and 2011, one of the most popular parks is <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Botanic_Gardens" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Botanic Gardens">Botanic Gardens</a><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Quarter,_Belfast" title="Queen&#39;s Quarter, Belfast">Queen\'s Quarter</a>. Built in the 1830s and designed by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lanyon" title="Charles Lanyon">Sir Charles Lanyon</a>, Botanic Gardens Palm House is one of the earliest examples of a curvilinear and cast iron <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">glasshouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Other attractions in the park include the Tropical Ravine, a humid jungle glen built in 1889, rose gardens and public events ranging from live opera broadcasts to pop concerts.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> played here in 1997. <a href="/wiki/Sir_Thomas_and_Lady_Dixon_Park" title="Sir Thomas and Lady Dixon Park">Sir Thomas and Lady Dixon Park</a>, to the south of the city centre, attracts thousands of visitors each year to its International Rose Garden.<sup id="cite_ref-Go_To_Belfast:_Sir_Thomas_and_Lady_Dixon_Park_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Go_To_Belfast:_Sir_Thomas_and_Lady_Dixon_Park-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Rose Week in July each year features over 20,000 blooms.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> It has an area of 128 acres (0.52&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of meadows, woodland and gardens and features a <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a> Memorial Garden, a <a href="/wiki/Japanese_garden" title="Japanese garden">Japanese garden</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Walled_garden" title="Walled garden">walled garden</a>, and the Golden Crown Fountain commissioned in 2002 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Golden Jubilee of Elizabeth II">Queen\'s Golden Jubilee</a> celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-Go_To_Belfast:_Sir_Thomas_and_Lady_Dixon_Park_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Go_To_Belfast:_Sir_Thomas_and_Lady_Dixon_Park-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, Belfast was named a finalist in the Large City (200,001 and over) category of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Horticultural_Society" title="Royal Horticultural Society">RHS</a> <a href="/wiki/Britain_in_Bloom" title="Britain in Bloom">Britain in Bloom</a> competition along with <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Croydon" title="London Borough of Croydon">London Borough of Croydon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Belfast_Zoo" title="Belfast Zoo">Belfast Zoo</a> is owned by Belfast City Council. The council spends \xc2\xa31.5&#160;million every year on running and promoting the zoo, which is one of the few local government-funded zoos in the UK and Ireland. The zoo is one of the top visitor attractions in Northern Ireland, receiving more than 295,000 visitors a year. The majority of the animals are in danger in their natural habitat. The zoo houses more than 1,200 animals of 140 species including <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbary_lion" title="Barbary lion">Barbary lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malayan_sun_bear" class="mw-redirect" title="Malayan sun bear">Malayan sun bears</a> (one of the few in the United Kingdom), two species of penguin, a family of <a href="/wiki/Western_lowland_gorilla" title="Western lowland gorilla">western lowland gorillas</a>, a troop of <a href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" class="mw-redirect" title="Common chimpanzee">common chimpanzees</a>, a pair of <a href="/wiki/Red_panda" title="Red panda">red pandas</a>, a pair of <a href="/wiki/Goodfellow%27s_tree-kangaroo" title="Goodfellow&#39;s tree-kangaroo">Goodfellow\'s tree-kangaroos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francois%27_langur" class="mw-redirect" title="Francois&#39; langur">Francois\' langurs</a>. The zoo also carries out important conservation work and takes part in European and international breeding programmes which help to ensure the survival of many species under threat.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Belfast" title="List of people from Belfast">List of people from Belfast</a></div>\n<table class="toccolours collapsible collapsed" style="width:15em;border-top-width:0;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+5.20%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left"><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_2001_census" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom 2001 census">2001 census</a>, the population was 276,459,<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Urban_Area_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Urban_Area-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> while 579,554 people lived in the wider <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Metropolitan Area">Belfast Metropolitan Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Metropolitan_Area_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Metropolitan_Area-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This made it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_United_Kingdom_settlements_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of largest United Kingdom settlements by population">fifteenth-largest city</a> in the United Kingdom, but the <a href="/wiki/List_of_conurbations_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="List of conurbations in the United Kingdom">eleventh-largest conurbation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belfast experienced a huge growth in population in the first half of the 20th century. This rise slowed and peaked around the start of the Troubles with the 1971 census showing almost 600,000 people in the Belfast Urban Area.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_in_Action_Urban_Growth_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_in_Action_Urban_Growth-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Since then, the inner city numbers have dropped dramatically as people have moved to swell the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Belfast">Greater Belfast</a> suburb population. The 2001 census population in the same Urban Area had fallen to 277,391<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Urban_Area_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Urban_Area-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> people, with 579,554 people living in the wider <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Metropolitan Area">Belfast Metropolitan Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Metropolitan_Area_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Metropolitan_Area-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2001 census recorded 81,650 people from Catholic backgrounds and 79,650 people from Protestant backgrounds of working age living in Belfast.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The population density in 2011 was 24.88 people/hectare (compared to 1.34 for the rest of Northern Ireland).<sup id="cite_ref-nisra_density_2011_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nisra_density_2011-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As with many cities, Belfast\'s inner city is currently characterised by the elderly, students and single young people, while families tend to live on the periphery. Socio-economic areas radiate out from the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Centre" title="Belfast City Centre">Central Business District</a>, with a pronounced wedge of affluence extending out the Malone Road and Upper Malone Road to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_in_Action_Urban_Growth_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_in_Action_Urban_Growth-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> An area of deprivation is found in the inner parts of the north and west of the city. The areas around the <a href="/wiki/Falls_Road,_Belfast" title="Falls Road, Belfast">Falls Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ardoyne" title="Ardoyne">Ardoyne</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Lodge,_Belfast" title="New Lodge, Belfast">New Lodge</a> (Catholic nationalist) and the <a href="/wiki/Shankill_Road" title="Shankill Road">Shankill Road</a> (Protestant loyalist) are among the ten most deprived wards in Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_murals_Ac.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Belfast_murals_Ac.jpg/220px-Belfast_murals_Ac.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Belfast_murals_Ac.jpg/330px-Belfast_murals_Ac.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Belfast_murals_Ac.jpg/440px-Belfast_murals_Ac.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_murals_Ac.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A loyalist mural in Belfast</div></div></div>\n<p>Despite a period of relative peace, most areas and districts of Belfast still reflect the divided nature of Northern Ireland as a whole. Many areas are still highly segregated along ethnic, political and religious lines, especially in working-class neighbourhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>These zones \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Irish_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Catholic">Catholic</a>/<a href="/wiki/Irish_Republicanism_in_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Republicanism in Northern Ireland">republican</a> on one side and <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ulster_loyalism" title="Ulster loyalism">loyalist</a> on the other \xe2\x80\x93 are invariably marked by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_flags_issue" title="Northern Ireland flags issue">flags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Irish_murals" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Irish murals">murals</a>. Segregation has been present throughout the history of Belfast but has been maintained and increased by each outbreak of violence in the city. This escalation in segregation, described as a "ratchet effect", has shown little sign of decreasing.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The highest levels of segregation in the city are in west Belfast with many areas greater than 90% Catholic. Opposite but comparatively high levels are seen in the predominantly Protestant east Belfast.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnic_Segregation_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnic_Segregation-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Areas where segregated working-class areas meet are known as <a href="/wiki/Interface_area" title="Interface area">interface areas</a> and sometimes marked by <a href="/wiki/Peace_lines" title="Peace lines">peace lines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> When violence flares, it tends to be in interface areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minorities_in_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic minorities in Northern Ireland">Ethnic minority</a> communities have been in Belfast since the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-Who_lives_here_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Who_lives_here-142">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The largest groups are Poles, Chinese and Indians.<sup id="cite_ref-QS208NI%20(a)_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS208NI_(a)-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KS201NI%20(a)_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KS201NI_(a)-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the expansion of the European Union, numbers have been boosted by an influx of Eastern European <a href="/wiki/Immigrants" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrants">immigrants</a>. Census figures (2011) showed that Belfast has a total non-white population of 10,219 or 3.3%,<sup id="cite_ref-KS201NI%20(a)_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KS201NI_(a)-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> while 18,420 or 6.6%<sup id="cite_ref-QS208NI%20(a)_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS208NI_(a)-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> of the population were born outside the UK and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-QS208NI%20(a)_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS208NI_(a)-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Almost half of those born outside the UK and Ireland live in <a href="/wiki/Belfast_South_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Belfast South (UK Parliament constituency)">south Belfast</a>, where they comprise 9.5% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-QS208NI%20(a)_143-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS208NI_(a)-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The majority of the estimated 5,000 Muslims<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and 200 <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> families<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> living in Northern Ireland live in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Belfast">Greater Belfast</a> area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_Census">2011 Census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2011 Census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On Census Day (27 March 2011) the usually resident population of Belfast Local Government District (2014) was 333,871 accounting for 18.44% of the NI total.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> This represents a 1.60% increase since the 2001 Census. \n</p><p>On Census Day 27 March 2011, in Belfast Local Government District (2014), considering the resident population:\n</p>\n<ul><li>3.23% were from an ethnic minority population and the remaining 96.77% were white (including Irish Traveller);</li>\n<li>48.82% belong to or were brought up in the Catholic faith and 42.47% belong to or were brought up in a \'Protestant and Other Christian (including Christian related)\'denomination; and</li>\n<li>43.32% indicated that they had a British national identity, 35.10% had an Irish national identity and 26.92% had a Northern Irish national identity.</li></ul>\n<p>Respondents could indicate more than one national identity\n</p><p>On Census Day 27 March 2011, in Belfast Local Government District (2014), considering the population aged 3 years old and over:\n</p>\n<ul><li>13.45% had some knowledge of Irish;</li>\n<li>5.23% had some knowledge of Ulster-Scots; and</li>\n<li>4.34% did not have English as their first language.</li></ul>\n<p>On Census Day 27 March 2011, considering the population aged 16 years old and over:\n</p>\n<ul><li>25.56% had a degree or higher qualification; while</li>\n<li>41.21% had no or low (Level 1*) qualifications.</li></ul>\n<p>Level 1 is 1\xe2\x80\x934 O Levels/CSE/GCSE (any grades) or equivalent\n</p><p>On Census Day 27 March 2011, considering the population aged 16 to 74 years old:\n</p>\n<ul><li>63.84% were economically active, 36.16% were economically inactive;</li>\n<li>52.90% were in paid employment; and</li>\n<li>5.59% were unemployed, of these 43.56% were long-term unemployed.</li></ul>\n<p>Long-term unemployed are those who stated that they have not worked since 2009 or earlier\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n\t<li class="gallerycaption">The Belfast City Council area in the 2011
