data-file-width="17284" data-file-height="16862" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Percentage born outside the UK and Ireland\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Belfast" title="Economy of Belfast">Economy of Belfast</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast%27s_Harland_and_Wolff_Shipyard_(RMS_Adriatic),_1907.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Belfast%27s_Harland_and_Wolff_Shipyard_%28RMS_Adriatic%29%2C_1907.jpg/220px-Belfast%27s_Harland_and_Wolff_Shipyard_%28RMS_Adriatic%29%2C_1907.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Belfast%27s_Harland_and_Wolff_Shipyard_%28RMS_Adriatic%29%2C_1907.jpg/330px-Belfast%27s_Harland_and_Wolff_Shipyard_%28RMS_Adriatic%29%2C_1907.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Belfast%27s_Harland_and_Wolff_Shipyard_%28RMS_Adriatic%29%2C_1907.jpg/440px-Belfast%27s_Harland_and_Wolff_Shipyard_%28RMS_Adriatic%29%2C_1907.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2086" data-file-height="1058" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast%27s_Harland_and_Wolff_Shipyard_(RMS_Adriatic),_1907.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1907 <a href="/wiki/Stereoscope" title="Stereoscope">stereoscope</a> postcard depicting the construction of a passenger liner (the RMS <i>Adriatic</i>) at the <a href="/wiki/Harland_and_Wolff" title="Harland and Wolff">Harland and Wolff</a> shipyard</div></div></div>\n<p>When the population of Belfast town began to grow in the 17th century, its economy was built on commerce.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_1_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_1-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> It provided a market for the surrounding countryside and the natural inlet of <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Lough" title="Belfast Lough">Belfast Lough</a> gave the city its own port. The port supplied an avenue for trade with Great Britain and later Europe and North America. In the mid-17th century, Belfast exported beef, butter, hides, tallow and corn and it imported coal, cloth, wine, brandy, paper, timber and tobacco.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_1_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_1-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Around this time, the linen trade in Northern Ireland blossomed and by the middle of the 18th century, one fifth of all the linen exported from Ireland was shipped from Belfast.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_1_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_1-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The present city however is a product of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> It was not until industry transformed the linen and shipbuilding trades that the economy and the population boomed. By the turn of the 19th century, Belfast had transformed into the largest linen producing centre in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_3_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_3-150">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> earning the nickname "<a href="/wiki/Linenopolis" title="Linenopolis">Linenopolis</a>".\n</p><p>Belfast harbour was dredged in 1845 to provide deeper berths for larger ships. Donegall Quay was built out into the river as the harbour was developed further and trade flourished.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_4_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_4-151">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Harland_and_Wolff" title="Harland and Wolff">Harland and Wolff</a> shipbuilding firm was created in 1861, and by the time the <i><a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" class="mw-redirect" title="RMS Titanic">Titanic</a></i> was built, in 1912, it had become the largest shipyard in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Titanic_in_History_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Titanic_in_History-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harlandandwolffcranes.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Harlandandwolffcranes.JPG/220px-Harlandandwolffcranes.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Harlandandwolffcranes.JPG/330px-Harlandandwolffcranes.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Harlandandwolffcranes.JPG/440px-Harlandandwolffcranes.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harlandandwolffcranes.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Samson_and_Goliath_(cranes)" title="Samson and Goliath (cranes)">Samson and Goliath</a>, Harland &amp; Wolff\'s gantry cranes</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Short_Brothers" title="Short Brothers">Short Brothers</a> plc is a British aerospace company based in Belfast. It was the first aircraft manufacturing company in the world. The company began its association with Belfast in 1936, with Short &amp; Harland Ltd, a venture jointly owned by Shorts and Harland and Wolff. Now known as Shorts Bombardier it works as an international aircraft manufacturer located near the Port of Belfast.<sup id="cite_ref-Corporate_Series_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corporate_Series-152">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The rise of mass-produced and cotton clothing following <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> were some of the factors which led to the decline of Belfast\'s international linen trade.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_3_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast,_The_Making_of_the_City_3-150">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Like many British cities dependent on traditional heavy industry, Belfast suffered serious decline since the 1960s, exacerbated greatly in the 1970s and 1980s by the Troubles. More than 100,000 manufacturing jobs have been lost since the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-Management_Today_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Management_Today-153">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> For several decades, Northern Ireland\'s fragile economy required significant public support from the <a href="/wiki/Exchequer" title="Exchequer">British exchequer</a> of up to \xc2\xa34&#160;billion per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Management_Today_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Management_Today-153">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_Troubles">After the Troubles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: After the Troubles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army#End_of_the_armed_campaign" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">IRA ceasefire</a> in 1994 and the signing of the Good Friday Agreement in 1998 have given investors increased confidence to invest in Belfast.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> This has led to a period of sustained economic growth and large-scale redevelopment of the city centre. Developments include <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Square,_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Square, Belfast">Victoria Square</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Quarter,_Belfast" title="Cathedral Quarter, Belfast">Cathedral Quarter</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Laganside" class="mw-redirect" title="Laganside">Laganside</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Odyssey_(Belfast)" class="mw-redirect" title="Odyssey (Belfast)">Odyssey</a> complex and the landmark <a href="/wiki/Waterfront_Hall" title="Waterfront Hall">Waterfront Hall</a>. </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterfront_Hall,_Belfast.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Waterfront_Hall%2C_Belfast.jpg/220px-Waterfront_Hall%2C_Belfast.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Waterfront_Hall%2C_Belfast.jpg/330px-Waterfront_Hall%2C_Belfast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Waterfront_Hall%2C_Belfast.jpg/440px-Waterfront_Hall%2C_Belfast.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="641" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterfront_Hall,_Belfast.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Waterfront Hall. Built in 1997, the hall is a concert, exhibition and conference venue.</div></div></div>\n<p>Other major developments include the regeneration of the <a href="/wiki/Titanic_Quarter,_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Titanic Quarter, Belfast">Titanic Quarter</a>, and the erection of the <a href="/wiki/Obel_Tower" title="Obel Tower">Obel Tower</a>, a skyscraper set to be the tallest tower on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\nToday, Belfast is Northern Ireland\'s educational and commercial hub. In February 2006, Belfast\'s unemployment rate stood at 4.2%, lower than both the Northern Ireland<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> and the UK average of 5.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Over the past 10 years employment has grown by 16.4%, compared with 9.2% for the UK as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Northern Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/Peace_dividend" title="Peace dividend">peace dividend</a> has led to soaring property prices in the city. In 2007, Belfast saw house prices grow by 50%, the fastest rate of growth in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> In March 2007, the average house in Belfast cost \xc2\xa391,819, with the average in south Belfast being \xc2\xa3141,000.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, Belfast had the lowest owner occupation rate in Northern Ireland at 54%.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Peace has boosted the numbers of tourists coming to Belfast. There were 6.4&#160;million visitors in 2005, which was a growth of 8.5% from 2004. The visitors spent \xc2\xa3285.2&#160;million, supporting more than 15,600 jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Visitor numbers rose by 6% to reach 6.8&#160;million in 2006, with tourists spending \xc2\xa3324&#160;million, an increase of 15% on 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s two airports have helped make the city one of the most visited weekend destinations in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belfast has been the fastest-growing economy of the thirty largest cities in the UK over the past decade, a new economy report by Howard Spencer has found. <i>"That\'s because [of] the fundamentals of the UK economy and [because] people actually want to invest in the UK,"</i> he commented on that report.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> Radio 4\'s World reported furthermore that despite higher levels of corporation tax in the UK than in the Republic. There are "huge amounts" of foreign investment coming into the country.\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> wrote about Belfast\'s growing economy: "According to the region\'s development agency, throughout the 1990s Northern Ireland had the fastest-growing regional economy in the UK, with GDP increasing 1 per cent per annum faster than the rest of the country. As with any modern economy, the service sector is vital to Northern Ireland\'s development and is enjoying excellent growth. In particular, the region has a booming tourist industry with record levels of visitors and tourist revenues and has established itself as a significant location for call centres."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times-167">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\nSince the ending of the region\'s conflict tourism has boomed in Northern Ireland, greatly aided by low cost.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times-167">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i>, a German weekly magazine for politics and economy, titled Belfast as <i>The New Celtic Tiger</i> which is "open for business".<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast-University-of-Ulster.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Belfast-University-of-Ulster.jpg/220px-Belfast-University-of-Ulster.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Belfast-University-of-Ulster.jpg/330px-Belfast-University-of-Ulster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Belfast-University-of-Ulster.jpg/440px-Belfast-University-of-Ulster.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1382" data-file-height="1037" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast-University-of-Ulster.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ulster_University" title="Ulster University">Ulster University</a>, Belfast campus</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast saw the worst of the Troubles in Northern Ireland, with nearly half of the total deaths in the conflict occurring in the city. However, since the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> in 1998, there has been significant <a href="/wiki/Urban_regeneration" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban regeneration">urban regeneration</a> in the city centre including Victoria Square, <a href="/wiki/Titanic_Quarter,_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Titanic Quarter, Belfast">Queen\'s Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laganside" class="mw-redirect" title="Laganside">Laganside</a> as well as the Odyssey complex and the landmark <a href="/wiki/Waterfront_Hall" title="Waterfront Hall">Waterfront Hall</a>. The city is served by two airports: The <a href="/wiki/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport" title="George Best Belfast City Airport">George Best Belfast City Airport</a> adjacent to Belfast Lough and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast International Airport</a> which is near <a href="/wiki/Lough_Neagh" title="Lough Neagh">Lough Neagh</a>. <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University_of_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s University of Belfast">Queen\'s University of Belfast</a> is the main university in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Ulster_University" title="Ulster University">Ulster University</a> also maintains a campus in the city, which concentrates on fine art, design and architecture.\n</p><p>Belfast is one of the constituent cities that makes up the <a href="/wiki/Dublin-Belfast_corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin-Belfast corridor">Dublin-Belfast corridor</a> region, which has a population of just under 3&#160;million.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SilentValley.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/SilentValley.jpg/220px-SilentValley.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/SilentValley.jpg/330px-SilentValley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/SilentValley.jpg/440px-SilentValley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SilentValley.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Silent Valley Reservoir, showing the brick-built overflow</div></div></div>\n<p>Most of Belfast\'s water is supplied via the <a href="/wiki/Mourne_Conduit" title="Mourne Conduit">Aquarius pipeline</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Silent_Valley_Reservoir" title="Silent Valley Reservoir">Silent Valley Reservoir</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_Down" title="County Down">County Down</a>, created to collect water from the <a href="/wiki/Mourne_Mountains" title="Mourne Mountains">Mourne Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The rest of the city\'s water is sourced from <a href="/wiki/Lough_Neagh" title="Lough Neagh">Lough Neagh</a>, via <i>Dunore Water Treatment Works</i> in County Antrim.<sup id="cite_ref-BMA_plan_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMA_plan-170">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The citizens of Belfast pay for their water in their <a href="/wiki/Rates_(tax)" title="Rates (tax)">rates</a> bill. Plans to bring in additional water tariffs have been deferred by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">devolution</a> in May 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Belfast has approximately 1,300&#160;km (808&#160;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Sanitary_sewer" title="Sanitary sewer">sewers</a>, which are currently being replaced in a project costing over \xc2\xa3100&#160;million and due for completion in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Power is provided from a number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_power_stations_in_Northern_Ireland" title="List of power stations in Northern Ireland">power stations</a> via <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Electricity" title="Northern Ireland Electricity">NIE Networks Limited</a> transmission lines. <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Natural_Gas" title="Phoenix Natural Gas">Phoenix Natural Gas Ltd.</a> started supplying customers in Larne and Greater Belfast with natural gas in 1996 via the newly constructed <a href="/wiki/Scotland-Northern_Ireland_pipeline" title="Scotland-Northern Ireland pipeline">Scotland-Northern Ireland pipeline</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BMA_plan_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMA_plan-170">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rates_(tax)" title="Rates (tax)">Rates</a> in Belfast (and the rest of Northern Ireland) were reformed in April 2007. The discrete <a href="/wiki/Capital_(economics)" title="Capital (economics)">capital</a> value system means rates bills are determined by the capital value of each domestic property as assessed by the <i>Valuation and Lands Agency</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The recent dramatic rise in house prices has made these reforms unpopular.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Health_and_Social_Care_Trust" title="Belfast Health and Social Care Trust">Belfast Health &amp; Social Care Trust</a> is one of five trusts that were created on 1 April 2007 by the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health,_Social_Services_and_Public_Safety" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Health, Social Services and Public Safety">Department of Health</a>. Belfast contains most of Northern Ireland\'s regional specialist centres.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Victoria_Hospital,_Belfast" title="Royal Victoria Hospital, Belfast">Royal Victoria Hospital</a> is an internationally renowned centre of excellence in trauma care and provides specialist trauma care for all of Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> It also provides the city\'s specialist <a href="/wiki/Neurosurgery" title="Neurosurgery">neurosurgical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ophthalmology" title="Ophthalmology">ophthalmology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otolaryngology" class="mw-redirect" title="Otolaryngology">ENT</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dentistry" title="Dentistry">dentistry</a> services. The <a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Hospital" title="Belfast City Hospital">Belfast City Hospital</a> is the regional specialist centre for haematology and is home to a cancer centre that rivals the best in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The Mary G McGeown Regional Nephrology Unit at the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_City_Hospital" title="Belfast City Hospital">City Hospital</a> is the kidney transplant centre and provides regional renal services for Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Musgrave_Park_Hospital" title="Musgrave Park Hospital">Musgrave Park Hospital</a> in south Belfast specialises in <a href="/wiki/Orthopedic_surgery" title="Orthopedic surgery">orthopaedics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rheumatology" title="Rheumatology">rheumatology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sports_medicine" title="Sports medicine">sports medicine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rehabilitation_psychology" title="Rehabilitation psychology">rehabilitation</a>. It is home to Northern Ireland\'s first Acquired Brain Injury Unit, costing \xc2\xa39&#160;million and opened by the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Duchess_of_Cornwall" title="Duchess of Cornwall">Duchess of Cornwall</a> in May 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Other hospitals in Belfast include the <a href="/wiki/Mater_Infirmorum_Hospital" title="Mater Infirmorum Hospital">Mater Hospital</a> in north Belfast and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Belfast_Hospital_for_Sick_Children" title="Royal Belfast Hospital for Sick Children">Children\'s Hospital</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Belfast" title="Transport in Belfast">Transport in Belfast</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_714574.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_714574.jpg/220px-George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_714574.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_714574.jpg/330px-George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_714574.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_714574.jpg/440px-George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_714574.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_714574.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport" title="George Best Belfast City Airport">George Best Belfast City Airport</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast is a relatively car-dependent city by European standards, with an extensive road network including the 22.5 miles (36&#160;km) <a href="/wiki/M2_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M2 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M2</a> and <a href="/wiki/M22_motorway_(Northern_Ireland)" title="M22 motorway (Northern Ireland)">M22 motorway</a> route.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> A 2005 survey of how people travel in Northern Ireland showed that people in Belfast made 77% of all journeys by car, 11% by public transport and 6% on foot.<sup id="cite_ref-Travel_Survey_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Travel_Survey-181">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> It showed that Belfast has 0.70 cars per household compared to figures of 1.18 in the East and 1.14 in the West of Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-Travel_Survey_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Travel_Survey-181">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> A road improvement-scheme in Belfast began early in 2006, with the upgrading of two junctions along the <a href="/wiki/Westlink_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Westlink Belfast">Westlink</a> dual-carriageway to <a href="/wiki/Grade_separation" title="Grade separation">grade-separated</a> standard. The improvement scheme was completed five months ahead of schedule in February 2009, with the official opening taking place on 4 March 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Commentators have argued that this may create a bottleneck at York Street, the next <a href="/wiki/At-grade_intersection" class="mw-redirect" title="At-grade intersection">at-grade intersection</a>, until that too is upgraded.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On 25 October 2012 the stage 2 report for the York Street intersection was approved<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> and in December 2012 the planned upgrade moved into stage 3 of the development process. If successfully completing the necessary statutory procedures, work on a grade separated junction to connect the Westlink to the M2/M3 motorways is scheduled to take place between 2014 and 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> creating a continuous link between the M1 and M2, the two main motorways in Northern Ireland.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gt_Victoria_Street_station,_Belfast_(9)_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2223181.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Gt_Victoria_Street_station%2C_Belfast_%289%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2223181.jpg/220px-Gt_Victoria_Street_station%2C_Belfast_%289%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2223181.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Gt_Victoria_Street_station%2C_Belfast_%289%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2223181.jpg/330px-Gt_Victoria_Street_station%2C_Belfast_%289%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2223181.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Gt_Victoria_Street_station%2C_Belfast_%289%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2223181.jpg/440px-Gt_Victoria_Street_station%2C_Belfast_%289%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2223181.jpg 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="407" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gt_Victoria_Street_station,_Belfast_(9)_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2223181.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Great_Victoria_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Victoria Street">Great Victoria Street</a> station on <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Railways">Northern Ireland Railways</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hackney_carriage" title="Hackney carriage">Black taxis</a> are common in the city, operating on a <a href="/wiki/Share_taxi" title="Share taxi">share</a> basis in some areas.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> These are outnumbered by <a href="/wiki/Taxicabs_of_the_United_Kingdom#Private_hire_(&#39;minicabs&#39;)" title="Taxicabs of the United Kingdom">private hire taxis</a>. Bus and rail public transport in Northern Ireland is operated by subsidiaries of <a href="/wiki/Translink_(Northern_Ireland)" title="Translink (Northern Ireland)">Translink</a>. Bus services in the city proper and the nearer suburbs are operated by <a href="/wiki/Metro_(Belfast)" title="Metro (Belfast)">Translink Metro</a>, with services focusing on linking residential districts with the city centre on 12 <a href="/wiki/Quality_bus_corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="Quality bus corridor">quality bus corridors</a> running along main radial roads,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>More distant suburbs are served by <a href="/wiki/Ulsterbus" title="Ulsterbus">Ulsterbus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Railways">Northern Ireland Railways</a> provides <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Suburban_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Suburban Rail">suburban services</a> along three lines running through Belfast\'s northern suburbs to <a href="/wiki/Carrickfergus" title="Carrickfergus">Carrickfergus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Larne" title="Larne">Larne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Larne_Harbour_railway_station" title="Larne Harbour railway station">Larne Harbour</a>, eastwards towards <a href="/wiki/Bangor,_County_Down" title="Bangor, County Down">Bangor</a> and south-westwards towards <a href="/wiki/Lisburn" title="Lisburn">Lisburn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portadown_railway_station" title="Portadown railway station">Portadown</a>. This service is known as the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Suburban_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Suburban Rail">Belfast Suburban Rail</a> system. Belfast is linked <a href="/wiki/Belfast-Derry_railway_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast-Derry railway line">directly</a> to <a href="/wiki/Coleraine_railway_station" title="Coleraine railway station">Coleraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portrush_railway_station" title="Portrush railway station">Portrush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Londonderry_railway_station" title="Londonderry railway station">Derry</a>. Belfast has a direct rail connection with <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Enterprise_(train)" class="mw-redirect" title="Enterprise (train)">Enterprise</a></i> which is operated jointly by NIR and <a href="/wiki/Iarnr%C3%B3d_%C3%89ireann" title="Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann">Iarnr\xc3\xb3d \xc3\x89ireann</a>, the state railway company of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>. There are no rail services to cities in other countries of the United Kingdom, due to the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea_fixed_crossing" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Sea fixed crossing">lack of a bridge or tunnel</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> to the island of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>. There is, however, a combined ferry and rail ticket between Belfast and cities in Great Britain, which is referred to as <i>Sailrail</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast-GliderBus-TitanicQuarter-P1510185.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Belfast-GliderBus-TitanicQuarter-P1510185.jpg/220px-Belfast-GliderBus-TitanicQuarter-P1510185.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Belfast-GliderBus-TitanicQuarter-P1510185.jpg/330px-Belfast-GliderBus-TitanicQuarter-P1510185.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Belfast-GliderBus-TitanicQuarter-P1510185.jpg/440px-Belfast-GliderBus-TitanicQuarter-P1510185.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast-GliderBus-TitanicQuarter-P1510185.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Glider_(Belfast)" title="Glider (Belfast)">Glider</a> bus rapid transit services opened in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In April 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Regional_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Department for Regional Development">Department for Regional Development</a> reported on a plan for a light-rail system, similar to that in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. The consultants said Belfast does not have the population to support a light rail system, suggesting that investment in bus-based rapid transit would be preferable. The study found that bus-based rapid transit produces positive economic results, but light rail does not. The report by Atkins &amp; KPMG, however, said there would be the option of migrating to light rail in the future should the demand increase.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city has two airports: <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast International Airport</a> offering, domestic, European and international flights such as Orlando operated seasonally by <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a>. The airport is located northwest of the city, near Lough Neagh, while the <a href="/wiki/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport" title="George Best Belfast City Airport">George Best Belfast City Airport</a>, which is closer to the city centre by train from <a href="/wiki/Sydenham_railway_station,_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Sydenham railway station, Northern Ireland">Sydenham</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Bangor,_County_Down" title="Bangor, County Down">Bangor</a> Line, adjacent to Belfast Lough, offers UK domestic flights and a few European flights. In 2005, Belfast International Airport was the 11th busiest commercial airport in the UK, accounting for just over 2% of all UK terminal passengers while the George Best Belfast City Airport was the 16th busiest and had 1% of UK terminal passengers. The Belfast \xe2\x80\x93 Liverpool route is the busiest domestic flight route in the UK excluding London with 555,224 passengers in 2009. Over 2.2&#160;million passengers flew between Belfast and London in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belfast has a large <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Belfast">port</a> used for exporting and importing goods, and for passenger ferry services. <a href="/wiki/Stena_Line" title="Stena Line">Stena Line</a> runs regular routes to <a href="/wiki/Cairnryan" title="Cairnryan">Cairnryan</a> in Scotland using its conventional vessels\xe2\x80\x94with a crossing time of around 2 hours 15 minutes. Until 2011 the route went to <a href="/wiki/Stranraer" title="Stranraer">Stranraer</a> and used inter alia a HSS (High Speed Service) vessel\xe2\x80\x94with a crossing time of around 90 minutes. Stena Line also operates a route to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>. A seasonal sailing to <a href="/wiki/Douglas,_Isle_of_Man" title="Douglas, Isle of Man">Douglas, Isle of Man</a> is operated by the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Steam_Packet" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle of Man Steam Packet">Isle of Man Steam Packet Company</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Glider_(Belfast)" title="Glider (Belfast)">Glider</a> bus service is a new form of transport in Belfast. Introduced in 2018, it is a rapid transit system linking East Belfast, West Belfast and the Titanic Quarter from the City Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Using <a href="/wiki/Articulated_buses" class="mw-redirect" title="Articulated buses">articulated buses</a>, the \xc2\xa390&#160;million service saw a 17% increase in its first month in Belfast, with 30,000 more people using the Gliders every week. The service is being recognised as helping to modernise the city\'s public transport.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Route_9" title="National Cycle Route 9">National Cycle Route 9</a> to <a href="/wiki/Newry" title="Newry">Newry</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> which will eventually connect with Dublin,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> starts in Belfast.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Belfast" title="Culture of Belfast">Culture of Belfast</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ACDC-Hughes-long_ago.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ACDC-Hughes-long_ago.jpg/220px-ACDC-Hughes-long_ago.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ACDC-Hughes-long_ago.jpg/330px-ACDC-Hughes-long_ago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ACDC-Hughes-long_ago.jpg/440px-ACDC-Hughes-long_ago.jpg 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ACDC-Hughes-long_ago.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/AC/DC" title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a> with <a href="/wiki/Bon_Scott" title="Bon Scott">Bon Scott</a> (centre) pictured with guitarist <a href="/wiki/Angus_Young" title="Angus Young">Angus Young</a> (left) and bassist <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Williams" title="Cliff Williams">Cliff Williams</a> (back), performing at the <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Hall" title="Ulster Hall">Ulster Hall</a> in August 1979</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast\'s population is evenly split between its Protestant and Catholic residents.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Urban_Area_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Urban_Area-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> These two distinct cultural communities have both contributed significantly to the city\'s culture. Throughout the Troubles, Belfast artists continued to express themselves through poetry, art and music. In the period since the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> in 1998, Belfast has begun a social, economic and cultural transformation giving it a growing international cultural reputation.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, Belfast had an unsuccessful bid for the 2008 <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a>. The bid was run by an independent company, <i>Imagine Belfast</i>, who boasted that it would "make Belfast the meeting place of Europe\'s legends, where the meaning of history and belief find a home and a sanctuary from caricature, parody and oblivion."<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> the bid may have been undermined by the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Belfast" title="History of Belfast">city\'s history</a> and volatile politics.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004\xe2\x80\x9305, art and cultural events in Belfast were attended by 1.8&#160;million people (400,000 more than the previous year). The same year, 80,000 people participated in culture and other arts activities, twice as many as in 2003\xe2\x80\x9304.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Cultural_Strategy_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Cultural_Strategy-198">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> A combination of relative peace, international investment and an active promotion of arts and culture is attracting more tourists to Belfast than ever before. In 2004\xe2\x80\x9305, 5.9&#160;million people visited Belfast, a 10% increase from the previous year, and spent \xc2\xa3262.5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Cultural_Strategy_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Cultural_Strategy-198">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Orchestra" title="Ulster Orchestra">Ulster Orchestra</a>, based in Belfast, is Northern Ireland\'s only full-time <a href="/wiki/Symphony_orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Symphony orchestra">symphony orchestra</a> and is well renowned in the United Kingdom. Founded in 1966, it has existed in its present form since 1981, when the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Northern_Ireland" title="BBC Northern Ireland">BBC Northern Ireland</a> Orchestra was disbanded.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> The music school of Queen\'s University is responsible for arranging a notable series of lunchtime and evening concerts, often given by renowned musicians which are usually given in The Harty Room at the university (University Square).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_emerging_from_the_Ritz_Cinema,_Fisherwick_Place,_Belfast_November_8,_1963.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/The_Beatles_emerging_from_the_Ritz_Cinema%2C_Fisherwick_Place%2C_Belfast_November_8%2C_1963.jpg/220px-The_Beatles_emerging_from_the_Ritz_Cinema%2C_Fisherwick_Place%2C_Belfast_November_8%2C_1963.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/The_Beatles_emerging_from_the_Ritz_Cinema%2C_Fisherwick_Place%2C_Belfast_November_8%2C_1963.jpg/330px-The_Beatles_emerging_from_the_Ritz_Cinema%2C_Fisherwick_Place%2C_Belfast_November_8%2C_1963.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/The_Beatles_emerging_from_the_Ritz_Cinema%2C_Fisherwick_Place%2C_Belfast_November_8%2C_1963.jpg/440px-The_Beatles_emerging_from_the_Ritz_Cinema%2C_Fisherwick_Place%2C_Belfast_November_8%2C_1963.jpg 2x" data-file-width="827" data-file-height="647" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Beatles_emerging_from_the_Ritz_Cinema,_Fisherwick_Place,_Belfast_November_8,_1963.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> emerging from the Ritz Cinema, Belfast following their concert, 8 November 1963.</div></div></div>\n<p>Musicians and bands who have written songs about or dedicated to Belfast include\n<a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Morrison" title="Van Morrison">Van Morrison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snow_Patrol" title="Snow Patrol">Snow Patrol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simple_Minds" title="Simple Minds">Simple Minds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rogue_Male_(band)" title="Rogue Male (band)">Rogue Male</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katie_Melua" title="Katie Melua">Katie Melua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boney_M" class="mw-redirect" title="Boney M">Boney M</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Muldoon" title="Paul Muldoon">Paul Muldoon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stiff_Little_Fingers" title="Stiff Little Fingers">Stiff Little Fingers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanci_Griffith" title="Nanci Griffith">Nanci Griffith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Patterson" title="Glenn Patterson">Glenn Patterson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orbital_(band)" title="Orbital (band)">Orbital</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">James Taylor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fun_Boy_Three" title="Fun Boy Three">Fun Boy Three</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spandau_Ballet" title="Spandau Ballet">Spandau Ballet</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Police" title="The Police">The Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnbrack" title="Barnbrack">Barnbrack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Moore" title="Gary Moore">Gary Moore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neon_Neon" title="Neon Neon">Neon Neon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toxic_Waste_(band)" title="Toxic Waste (band)">Toxic Waste</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_Orchard" title="Energy Orchard">Energy Orchard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Bragg" title="Billy Bragg">Billy Bragg</a>.\n</p><p>Belfast has a longstanding underground club scene which was established in the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belfast has the highest concentration of Irish-speakers in Northern Ireland. Like all areas of the island of Ireland outside of the <a href="/wiki/Gaeltacht" title="Gaeltacht">Gaeltacht</a>, the Irish language in Belfast is not that of an unbroken intergenerational transmission. Due to community activity in the 1960s, including the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Shaw%27s_Road" title="Shaw&#39;s Road">Shaw\'s Road Gaeltacht</a> community, the expanse in the Irish language arts, and the advancements made in the availability of Irish medium education throughout the city, it can now be said that there is a \'mother-tongue\' community of speakers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (November 2010)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Belfast#Dubious" title="Talk:Belfast">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> The language is heavily promoted in the city and is particularly visible in the Falls Road area, where the signs on both the iconic black taxis and on the public buses are bilingual.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Projects to promote the language in the city are funded by various sources, notably <a href="/wiki/Foras_na_Gaeilge" title="Foras na Gaeilge">Foras na Gaeilge</a>, an all-Ireland body funded by both the Irish and British governments. There are a number of Irish language Primary schools and one secondary school in Belfast. The provision of certain resources for these schools (for example, such as the provision of textbooks) is supported by the charitable organisation TACA.\n</p><p>In late August 2018, at least three groups were vying for the right to purchase the 5,500 <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" class="mw-redirect" title="RMS Titanic">RMS Titanic</a> relics that were an asset of the bankrupt <a href="/wiki/Premier_Exhibitions" title="Premier Exhibitions">Premier Exhibitions</a>. One of the offers was by a group including the <a href="/wiki/National_Maritime_Museum" title="National Maritime Museum">National Maritime Museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Museums_Northern_Ireland" title="National Museums Northern Ireland">National Museums Northern Ireland</a>, with assistance by <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">James Cameron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Oceanographer <a href="/wiki/Robert_Ballard" title="Robert Ballard">Robert Ballard</a> said he favored this bid since it would ensure that the memorabilia would be permanently displayed in Belfast (where the Titanic was built) and in <a href="/wiki/Greenwich" title="Greenwich">Greenwich</a>. A decision as to the outcome was to be made by a <a href="/wiki/United_States_district_court" title="United States district court">United States district court</a> judge.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_Telegraph,_July_2010_(01).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Belfast_Telegraph%2C_July_2010_%2801%29.JPG/220px-Belfast_Telegraph%2C_July_2010_%2801%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Belfast_Telegraph%2C_July_2010_%2801%29.JPG/330px-Belfast_Telegraph%2C_July_2010_%2801%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Belfast_Telegraph%2C_July_2010_%2801%29.JPG/440px-Belfast_Telegraph%2C_July_2010_%2801%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belfast_Telegraph,_July_2010_(01).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The former <i><a href="/wiki/Belfast_Telegraph" title="Belfast Telegraph">Belfast Telegraph</a></i> headquarters</div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast is the home of the <i><a href="/wiki/Belfast_Telegraph" title="Belfast Telegraph">Belfast Telegraph</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Irish_News" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish News">Irish News</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_News_Letter" title="The News Letter">The News Letter</a></i>, the oldest <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English-language</a> daily newspaper in the world still in publication.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/BBC_Northern_Ireland" title="BBC Northern Ireland">BBC Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> station <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulster Television">UTV</a> and commercial radio stations <a href="/wiki/Q_Radio_Belfast" title="Q Radio Belfast">Q Radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/U105" title="U105">U105</a>. Two community radio stations, <a href="/wiki/Blast_106" title="Blast 106">Blast 106</a> and Irish-language station <a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_F%C3%A1ilte" title="Raidi\xc3\xb3 F\xc3\xa1ilte">Raidi\xc3\xb3 F\xc3\xa1ilte</a>, broadcast to the city from west Belfast, as does <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Radio" title="Queen&#39;s Radio">Queen\'s Radio</a>, a student-run radio station which broadcasts from <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University_Belfast_Students%27_Union" title="Queen&#39;s University Belfast Students&#39; Union">Queen\'s University Students\' Union</a>.\n</p><p>One of Northern Ireland\'s two community TV stations, <a href="/wiki/NvTv" class="mw-redirect" title="NvTv">NvTv</a>, is based in the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Quarter,_Belfast" title="Cathedral Quarter, Belfast">Cathedral Quarter</a> of the city. There are two independent cinemas in Belfast: the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Film_Theatre" title="Queen&#39;s Film Theatre">Queen\'s Film Theatre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Strand_Cinema" title="Strand Cinema">Strand Cinema</a>, which host screenings during the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Film_Festival" title="Belfast Film Festival">Belfast Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Festival_at_Queen%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Belfast Festival at Queen&#39;s">Belfast Festival at Queen\'s</a>. Broadcasting only over the Internet is Homely Planet, the Cultural Radio Station for Northern Ireland, supporting community relations.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city has become a popular film location; The Paint Hall at Harland and Wolff has become one of the UK Film Council\'s main studios. The facility comprises four stages of 16,000 square feet (1,500&#160;m<sup>2</sup>). Shows filmed at The Paint Hall include the film <i><a href="/wiki/City_of_Ember" title="City of Ember">City of Ember</a></i> (2008) and <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a></i> series (beginning in late 2009).\n</p><p>In November 2011, Belfast became the smallest city to host the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV Europe Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> The event was hosted by <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a> and celebrities such as <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessie_J" title="Jessie J">Jessie J</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hayden_Panettiere" title="Hayden Panettiere">Hayden Panettiere</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> travelled to Northern Ireland to attend the event, held in the <a href="/wiki/Odyssey_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Odyssey Arena">Odyssey Arena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Belfast&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Belfast" title="Sport in Belfast">Sport in Belfast</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kingspan_Stadium,_Belfast.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Kingspan_Stadium%2C_Belfast.jpg/220px-Kingspan_Stadium%2C_Belfast.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Kingspan_Stadium%2C_Belfast.jpg/330px-Kingspan_Stadium%2C_Belfast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Kingspan_Stadium%2C_Belfast.jpg/440px-Kingspan_Stadium%2C_Belfast.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2688" data-file-height="1520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kingspan_Stadium,_Belfast.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ravenhill_Stadium" title="Ravenhill Stadium">Ravenhill Stadium</a> is the home of <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Rugby" title="Ulster Rugby">Ulster Rugby</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Belfast has several notable sports teams playing a diverse variety of sports such as <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_games" title="Gaelic games">Gaelic games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Marathon" title="Belfast Marathon">Belfast Marathon</a> is run annually on May Day, and attracted 20,000 participants in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Marathon_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Marathon-209">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Northern Ireland national football team">Northern Ireland national football team</a>, ranked 23rd in August 2017 in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA World Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (January 2021)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> plays its home matches at <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Park" title="Windsor Park">Windsor Park</a>. The 2017\xe2\x80\x9318 <a href="/wiki/NIFL_Premiership" title="NIFL Premiership">Irish League</a> champions <a href="/wiki/Crusaders_F.C." title="Crusaders F.C.">Crusaders</a> are based at <a href="/wiki/Seaview_(football_ground)" title="Seaview (football ground)">Seaview</a>, in the north of the city. Other <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_football_system#Senior" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland football system">senior</a> clubs are <a href="/wiki/Glentoran_F.C." title="Glentoran F.C.">Glentoran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linfield_F.C." title="Linfield F.C.">Linfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cliftonville_F.C." title="Cliftonville F.C.">Cliftonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harland_%26_Wolff_Welders_F.C." title="Harland &amp; Wolff Welders F.C.">Harland &amp; Wolff Welders</a> and <a href="/wiki/PSNI_F.C." title="PSNI F.C.">PSNI</a>. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_football_system#Intermediate" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland football system">Intermediate-level</a> clubs are: <a href="/wiki/Dundela_F.C." title="Dundela F.C.">Dundela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newington_Youth_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Newington Youth F.C.">Newington Youth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University_A.F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s University A.F.C.">Queen\'s University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sport_%26_Leisure_Swifts_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Sport &amp; Leisure Swifts F.C.">Sport &amp; Leisure Swifts</a>, who compete in the <a href="/wiki/NIFL_Premier_Intermediate_League" title="NIFL Premier Intermediate League">NIFL Premier Intermediate League</a>; <a href="/wiki/Albert_Foundry_F.C." title="Albert Foundry F.C.">Albert Foundry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bloomfield_F.C." title="Bloomfield F.C.">Bloomfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colin_Valley_F.C." title="Colin Valley F.C.">Colin Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crumlin_Star_F.C." title="Crumlin Star F.C.">Crumlin Star</a>, Dunmurry Rec., Dunmurry Young Men, <a href="/wiki/East_Belfast_F.C." title="East Belfast F.C.">East Belfast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grove_United_F.C." title="Grove United F.C.">Grove United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Immaculata_F.C." title="Immaculata F.C.">Immaculata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iveagh_United_F.C." title="Iveagh United F.C.">Iveagh United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malachians_F.C." title="Malachians F.C.">Malachians</a>, Orangefield Old Boys, <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Youth_Club_F.C." title="Rosario Youth Club F.C.">Rosario Youth Club</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Luke%27s_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="St Luke&#39;s F.C. (page does not exist)">St Luke\'s</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_Young_Men_F.C." title="St Patrick&#39;s Young Men F.C.">St Patrick\'s Young Men</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shankill_United_F.C." title="Shankill United F.C.">Shankill United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Short_Brothers_F.C." title="Short Brothers F.C.">Short Brothers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sirocco_Works_F.C." title="Sirocco Works F.C.">Sirocco Works</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Amateur_Football_League" title="Northern Amateur Football League">Northern Amateur Football League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brantwood_F.C." title="Brantwood F.C.">Brantwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donegal_Celtic" class="mw-redirect" title="Donegal Celtic">Donegal Celtic</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ballymena_%26_Provincial_Football_League" title="Ballymena &amp; Provincial Football League">Ballymena &amp; Provincial League</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Belfast was the home town of former <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> player <a href="/wiki/George_Best" title="George Best">George Best</a>, the 1968 <a href="/wiki/European_Footballer_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="European Footballer of the Year">European Footballer of the Year</a>, who died in November 2005. On the day he was buried in the city, 100,000 people lined the route from his home on the Cregagh Road to Roselawn cemetery.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Since his death the <a href="/wiki/George_Best_Belfast_City_Airport" title="George Best Belfast City Airport">City Airport</a> was named after him and a trust has been set up to fund a memorial to him in the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belfast is home to over twenty <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_football" title="Gaelic football">Gaelic football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurling" title="Hurling">hurling</a> clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Casement_Park" title="Casement Park">Casement Park</a> in west Belfast, home to the <a href="/wiki/Antrim_GAA" title="Antrim GAA">Antrim</a> county teams, has a capacity of 32,000 which makes it the second largest <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a> ground in <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> In May 2020, the foundation of <a href="/wiki/East_Belfast_GAA" title="East Belfast GAA">East Belfast GAA</a> returned Gaelic Games to unionist East Belfast after decades of its absence in the area. The current club president is Irish-language enthusiast <a href="/wiki/Linda_Ervine" title="Linda Ervine">Linda Ervine</a> who comes from a unionist background in the area. The team currently plays in the Down Senior County League.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1999 <a href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a> champions <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Rugby" title="Ulster Rugby">Ulster Rugby</a> play at <a href="/wiki/Ravenhill_Stadium" title="Ravenhill Stadium">Ravenhill Stadium</a> in the south of the city. Belfast has four teams in rugby\'s <a href="/wiki/All-Ireland_League_(rugby_union)" title="All-Ireland League (rugby union)">All-Ireland League</a>: <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Harlequins" title="Belfast Harlequins">Belfast Harlequins</a> in Division 1B; and <a href="/wiki/Instonians" title="Instonians">Instonians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University_RFC" title="Queen&#39;s University RFC">Queen\'s University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malone_RFC" title="Malone RFC">Malone</a> in Division 2A.\n</p><p>Belfast is home to the <a href="/wiki/Stormont_(cricket_ground)" title="Stormont (cricket ground)">Stormont cricket ground</a> since 1949 and was the venue for the <a href="/wiki/Irish_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish cricket team">Irish cricket team</a>\'s first ever <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day International</a> (ODI) against <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, Pro Wrestling Ulster formed. This is wrestling promotion on the independent circuit, holding events and PPVs in <a href="/wiki/Europa_Hotel,_Belfast" title="Europa Hotel, Belfast">Europa Hotel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandela_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandela Hall">The Mandela Hall</a>. It runs to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Belfast is home to one of the biggest British <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> clubs, the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Giants" title="Belfast Giants">Belfast Giants</a>. The Giants were founded in 2000 and play their games at the 9,500 capacity Odyssey Arena, where crowds normally range from 4,000 to 7,000. Many ex-NHL players have featured on the Giants roster, none more famous than world superstar <a href="/wiki/Theo_Fleury" class="mw-redirect" title="Theo Fleury">Theo Fleury</a>. The Giants play in the 10-team professional <a href="/wiki/Elite_Ice_Hockey_League" title="Elite Ice Hockey League">Elite Ice Hockey League</a> which is the top league in Britain. The Giants have been <a href="/wiki/British_ice_hockey_league_champions" title="British ice hockey league champions">league champions</a> 5 times, most recently in the 2018\xe2\x80\x9319 season. The <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Giants" title="Belfast Giants">Belfast Giants</a> are a huge brand in Northern Ireland and their increasing stature in the game led to the <a href="/wiki/Belfast_Giants" title="Belfast Giants">Belfast Giants</a> playing the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a> of the <a href="/wiki/NHL" class="mw-redirect" title="NHL">NHL</a> on 2 October 2010 at the Odyssey Arena in Belfast, losing the game 5\xe2\x80\x931.\n</p><p>Other significant sportspeople from Belfast include double world snooker champion <a href="/wiki/Alex_Higgins" title="Alex Higgins">Alex "Hurricane" Higgins</a><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> and world champion boxers <a href="/wiki/Wayne_McCullough" title="Wayne McCullough">Wayne McCullough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rinty_Monaghan" title="Rinty Monaghan">Rinty Monaghan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Frampton" title="Carl Frampton">Carl Frampton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\nLeander A.S.C is a well known swimming club in Belfast. Belfast produced the Formula One racing stars <a href="/wiki/John_Watson_(racing_driver)" title="John Watson (racing driver)">John Watson</a> who raced for five different teams during his career in the 1970s and 1980s and Ferrari driver <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Irvine" title="Eddie Irvine">Eddie Irvine</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span
